Leaving Prayer Space Due to Suspected Hadath Invalidates Prayer
Ruling on leaving mosque due to suspicion of hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on leaving the mosque or prayer rows due to suspicion of hadath and apply the concept of majlis muttahid to determine prayer validity.

Core Idea
Leaving the unified prayer space based on suspicion invalidates the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario where a person suspects hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer. The Hanafi school emphasizes the continuity of the prayer space, considering the mosque interior or the rows in an open area as one unified assembly (majlis muttahid). Unnecessary departure from this space based on mere suspicion breaks the prayer's continuity, rendering it invalid. However, if the person remains within the rows and realizes the mistake, the prayer remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The passage describes two situations: leaving the mosque due to suspicion of hadath, and leaving the rows in an open area (desert/field) due to suspicion. Note that no actual hadath occurred.
The suspicion is not a valid excuse.
2
State the ruling for exiting the mosque
If a person leaves the mosque based on suspicion, the prayer becomes invalid (fāsid).
The mosque interior is a unified space; leaving it breaks continuity.
3
State the ruling for exiting rows in an open area
If a person passes through all the rows and exits, prayer becomes invalid. But if he is still within the rows when he remembers no hadath occurred, he can continue and the prayer is valid.
The rows themselves are considered a unified space; leaving the entire row set invalidates.
4
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'līl)
The reason is the concept of majlis muttahid: inside the mosque, the entire building is treated as one place; in the open, the rows form a unified assembly. As long as one remains within this unit, the prayer's continuity is preserved.
This ruling applies only to unnecessary departure; actual hadath permits leaving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۳۵) حدث کے گمان سے مسجد سے باہر نکلا ، اور مسجد کے علاوہ میں حدث کے گمان سے صفوں سے باہر نکل گیا۔ تشریح : حدث ہوا نہیں تھا لیکن حدث کے گمان سے مسجد سے باہر نکل گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔اور اگر مسجد کے علاوہ مثلا صحراء، یا میدان میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہے تو جتنی صفیں ہیں ان سے گزر کر باہر ہو جائے تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، اور اگر ابھی صف کے درمیان تھا کہ یاد آیا کہ حدث نہیں ہوا ہے اور بنا کر لیا تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : مسجد کے اندر اندر گویا کہ مجلس متحد ہے ، اسی طرح صحراء اور میدان میں صف کے اندراندرمجلس متحد ہے اس لئے اس کی گنجائش ہوگی ۔
Translation (535): He left the mosque due to suspicion of hadath, and outside the mosque, due to suspicion of hadath, he went out of the rows. Explanation: Hadath had not occurred, but due to suspicion, he left the mosque, so prayer becomes invalid. And if he is praying outside the mosque, e.g., in a desert or field, and he passes through all the rows and goes out, prayer becomes invalid. But if he is still within the rows and remembers that hadath did not occur, and he builds upon it, then prayer is valid. Reason: Inside the mosque, the congregation is considered as one unit; similarly, in the desert or field, the rows are considered one unit, so there is concession for that.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This ruling covers two scenarios: leaving the mosque due to suspicion of hadath, and leaving the prayer rows in an open area. In both, if one exits the place of prayer (mosque or rows) based on a mistaken suspicion, the prayer becomes invalid because unnecessary departure from the prayer space breaks the continuity. However, if the person is still within the rows and realizes the mistake, he can return and continue. The reason given is that the mosque interior is considered one unified space for the prayer, and similarly the rows in the open are seen as one unit; staying within that unit allows building.

Key Terms
مجلس متحد (majlis muttahid): Unified assembly; the mosque interior or the prayer rows are treated as one continuous place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If during prayer in a desert, a person passes through all the rows to the back based on suspicion of hadath, then returns immediately upon realizing no hadath, what is the ruling?
A) Valid because he returned quickly.
B) Invalid because he left the rows.
C) Valid if he did not speak.
D) Invalid only if he intended to break prayer.

Key Takeaway
Leaving the unified prayer space (mosque or rows) based on mere suspicion invalidates the prayer; the continuity of the prayer space is a condition for validity.

When Turning from Qibla Invalidates Prayer: Recurring vs. Non-Recurring Events
Ruling on invalidating prayer by turning away due to false assumptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that only recurring events excuse turning from the qibla, and identify when a false assumption about wudu, masah, missed prayer, or impurity invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Only recurring events allow turning from qibla; false assumptions about non-recurring events invalidate prayer.

This passage from Thamarat al-Najah presents four scenarios where a person turns away from the qibla during prayer based on a false assumption. The author explains the underlying Hanafi principle: only events that occur repeatedly (hadath bar bar) permit turning away; any non-recurring assumption, even if sincere, renders the prayer invalid. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing when a prayer must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Turning away from the qibla during prayer is generally a mufsid (invalidator) unless excused. Here, the ruling is fasid for all four scenarios.
The act is turning away based on a false assumption.
2
Locate the underlying principle
The commentary states: 'The principle is that only recurring events (hadath bar bar) allow turning away; otherwise not.' So the key condition is recurrence.
Recurring events include frequent passing wind, nosebleeds, etc.
3
Classify each scenario
Determine whether the assumed event is recurring or non-recurring. All four (no wudu, expired masah, missed prayer, impurity) are non-recurring (occasional).
None of these are events that happen repeatedly in a person's normal state.
4
Apply the principle
Since none are recurring, turning away is not excused, and the prayer becomes fasid (invalid).
The prayer must be repeated or compensated.
5
Note the mufta bihi
This is the standard Hanafi position as per Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
Other schools may have different views, but this is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۳۶) وانصرافه ظانا انه غير متوضئ وانّ مدة مسحه انقضت او انّ عليه فائتة او نجاسة وان لم يخرج من المسجد

ترجمه : (۵۳۶) اس گمان سے کہ وضو والا نہیں ہے قبلے سے پھر گیا۔ یا اس گمان سے کہ مسح کی مدت ختم ہو گئی ، یا اس گمان سے کہ اس پر فوت شدہ نماز ہے ، یا اس پر نجاست ہے، اگر چہ مسجد سے نہ نکلا ہو۔ [ تب بھی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ]

تشريح : ان مسئلوں میں اصول یہ ہے کہ ۔ جو حدث بار بار پیش آتے ہیں، جیسے حدث ہونا، نکسیر پھوٹنا اس میں قبلے سے پھر جانے کی گنجائش ملے گی اس کے علاوہ میں نہیں ۔ یہاں اس اصول پر ہم مسئلے ہیں ۔ [1] آدمی اس گمان میں قبلے سے پھر گیا کہ اس کو شروع سے وضو ہی نہیں ہے، چاہے وہ مسجد سے باہر نہ نکلا ہو، تو یہ حدث ہونا نہیں ہے جو بار بار پیش آتا ہو اس لئے اس میں نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔[۲] نماز میں یہ خیال ہوا کہ مدت مسح ختم ہو گئی اس لئے قبلے سے پھر گیا تو یہ بار بار پیش آنے والا حدث نہیں ہے - [۳] آدمی صاحب ترتیب تھا نماز میں اس کو خیال آیا فوت شدہ نماز رہ گئی ہے اس لئے پہلے اس کو ادا کروں ، اس خیال سے قبلے سے پھر گیا، بعد میں یاد آیا کہ فوت شدہ نماز اس کے ذمے نہیں ہے تو نماز فاسد ہوگئی اس لئے یہ واقعہ کبھی کبھار ہوتا ہے۔ [۴] نماز میں یہ خیال ہوا کہ مجھ پر نجاست لگی ہوئی ہے جسکی بنا پر قبلے سے پھر گیاتو نماز ٹوٹ گئی اس لئے کہ یہ کبھی کبھار کا واقعہ ہے۔
(536) And his turning away, thinking that he does not have wudu, or that the duration of his wipe (masah) has expired, or that there is a missed prayer upon him, or that there is impurity, even if he did not exit the mosque.

Translation: (536) He turned away from the qibla thinking that he is not in a state of wudu, or thinking that the period of masah has expired, or thinking that he has a missed prayer, or thinking that he has impurity, even if he did not leave the mosque. [Then also the prayer becomes invalid.]

Commentary: The principle in these issues is that recurring events, such as passing wind or nosebleed, allow turning away from the qibla; otherwise not. Here are four cases: [1] He turned away thinking he never had wudu—this is not a recurring event, so prayer invalidates. [2] He thought the masah period expired—also not recurring. [3] He was a person of order (sahib tartib) and thought he had a missed prayer, so he turned away to pray it first, then remembered it was not due—invalidates because it's occasional. [4] He thought he had impurity on him and turned away—invalidates because it's occasional.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling statement with explanatory commentary (sharh) on when turning away from the qibla invalidates prayer. The author lists four scenarios where a person turns away from the qibla due to a false assumption about a non-recurring event (hadath). The underlying principle is that only recurring events (like passing wind or nosebleeds) permit turning away; non-recurring assumptions invalidate the prayer. Each case is explained: (1) thinking one has no wudu, (2) thinking masah period expired, (3) thinking a missed prayer is due, (4) thinking there is impurity. All are non-recurring assumptions, so the prayer becomes fasid (invalid).

Key Terms
مفسد الصلوة (mufsid al-salah): An action or event that invalidates the prayer, requiring its repetition or compensation.
حدث بار بار (hadath bar bar): A recurring event such as passing wind or nosebleed that frequently occurs, providing a concession to turn away from qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person turns away from the qibla thinking he has impurity on him, but it was a false assumption, what happens to his prayer?
A) Prayer is still valid because he thought he was cleansing himself.
B) Prayer is invalid because it was a non-recurring assumption.
C) Prayer is valid if he remains inside the mosque.
D) Prayer becomes wajib to repeat with sujood as-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Turning away from the qibla based on a false assumption about a non-recurring event invalidates the prayer; only genuine recurring events excuse this action.

Prompting Others than the Imam
Ruling on prompting (talaqin) someone other than one's imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prompting (talaqin) during prayer and identify the evidence for the distinction between one's own imam and others.

Core Idea
Prompting anyone other than your imam during prayer invalidates it; prompting your own imam is only allowed for correction.

This passage addresses a common situation during congregational prayer: when someone forgets a verse, another worshipper may want to correct him. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between correcting your own imam (the one you are following) and correcting another person. The key principle is that prompting should only serve to fix one's own prayer, not others'. Let us examine the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is prompting (talaqin) someone other than one's imam during prayer. The ruling according to the Hanafi school is that the prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
The act is considered like unnecessary speech, which invalidates prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ali (ra) that the Prophet forbade prompting the imam (لا تفتح على الامام), as well as an athar equating it to speech. A second hadith allows prompting one's own imam when he forgets.
These evidences are from Sunan Abi Dawud and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition (nahy) in 'la taftha' indicates that the act is generally forbidden. However, necessity (correction of one's own prayer) creates an exception for one's own imam. For others, there is no necessity, so the prohibition remains.
Hanafi usul: al-nahy yufidu al-tahrim unless there is a valid reason.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools allow prompting in all cases if it is to correct the recitation. The Hanafi school restricts it to one's own imam only, based on the specific evidence and the principle of avoiding unnecessary speech.
The practical difference: a Shafi'i may allow prompting any person, while a Hanafi would consider it invalid if the prompted person is not his imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۳۷) وفتحه على غير امامه

ترجمه : (۵۳۷) اپنے امام کے سوا دوسرے کو لقمہ دینا۔

تشریح : اپنے امام کو لقمہ دینا تعلیم اور تعلیم ہے اس لئے اس کی اجازت نہیں ہونی چاہئے ،لیکن چونکہ اس سے اپنی نماز کی اصلاح ہے اس لئے اس کی اجازت دی گئی ہے، لیکن دوسرے آدمی کو لقمہ دینے میں اپنی نماز کی اصلاح نہیں ہے اور نہ اس کی ضرورت ہے اس لئے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔

وجه : (۱) لقمہ دینے کی ممانعت ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن على قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يا علي ! لا تفتح على الامام في الصلوة - (ابوداود شریف، باب انھی عن التلقین ، ص ۱۳۹، نمبر ۹۰۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت نہ ہو تو لقمہ نہیں دینا چاہئے ۔ (۲) ان عليا قال : لا تفتح على الامام قوم و هو يقرأ فانه كلام - (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب تلقینۃ الامام، ج ثانی، ص۱۹۲، نمبر ۲۸۲۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ لقمہ دینا کلام کرنے کے درجے میں ہے اسلئے بلا ضرورت لقمہ نہیں دینا چاہئے ۔ (۳) مجبوری میں اپنے امام کو لقمہ دینے کی گنجائش اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن المسور بن يزيد المالكي أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم - قال يحيى - و ربما قال: شهدت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقرأ في الصلوة فترک شيئاً لم يقرأه ، فقال له رجل: يا رسول الله تركت آية كذا و كذا فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : هلا ذكرتنيها - (ابوداود شریف ، باب الفتح على الامام فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۳۹، نمبر ۹۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اپنا امام بھول جائے تو اسکولقمہ دیا جا سکتا ہے۔ (۴) اثر میں ہے کہ لقمہ مانگے تو لقمہ دے۔ عن ابی عبد الرحمن السلمي قال : اذا استطعمكم فأطعموه ، يقول اذا تعايا فردوا عليه (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب تلقیۃ الامام، ج ثانی، ص ۹۳ نمبر ۲۸۳۴ رسنن بیھقی ، باب اذا حصر الامام لقن ، ج ثالث ص ۳۰۰ نمبر ۵۷۹۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ لقمہ مانگے تو لقمہ دے ورنہ نہیں۔
(537) And his prompting (fath) someone other than his imam.

Translation: (537) Prompting (giving a cue/luqma) to someone other than one's own imam.

Commentary: Prompting one's own imam is teaching and [should not be allowed], but because it corrects one's own prayer, it is permitted. However, prompting another person does not correct one's own prayer and is not needed, so the prayer becomes invalid.

Evidence: (1) Prohibition of prompting: Hadith from Ali that the Prophet said: 'O Ali! Do not prompt the imam during prayer.' (2) Ali also said: 'Do not prompt the imam while he is reciting, for it is speech.' (3) Concession for prompting one's imam in necessity: Hadith from Miswar ibn Yazid al-Maliki that the Prophet omitted something in recitation, and a man reminded him, and the Prophet said: 'Why didn't you remind me?' (4) Athar: If the imam asks for prompting, then prompt; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) about prompting (talaqin) during prayer. The Hanafi position: prompting anyone other than your own imam invalidates the prayer because it does not serve to correct your own prayer. Prompting your own imam is permitted only for correction when the imam forgets. The author provides four pieces of evidence: (1) a hadith prohibiting prompting the imam generally, (2) an athar equating prompting to speech (which invalidates prayer), (3) a hadith allowing prompting one's own imam when needed, and (4) an athar that if the imam requests prompting, it is allowed. Thus, the default ruling is prohibition unless there is necessity and it is one's own imam.

Key Terms
لقمة (luqma): Prompting or cueing the imam (or another) by reciting the correct verse when he forgets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person prompts a fellow worshipper who is not his imam during prayer?
A) The prayer remains valid but makruh.
B) The prayer becomes invalid (fasid) because it does not correct one's own prayer.
C) The prayer becomes valid only if the prompted person responds.
D) The prayer becomes invalid only if the imam was reciting correctly.

Key Takeaway
Prompting anyone other than your imam during prayer invalidates it; prompting your own imam is permitted only for necessary correction.

Takbir with Intention to Transfer to Another Prayer
Ruling with proof on intentional transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when someone intentionally leaves a prayer for another and distinguish it from the case of a mistaken salam.

Core Idea
Intentionally leaving a prayer for another invalidates the first; accidental leaving allows building due to common need.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a person in the middle of a fard prayer suddenly decides to pray a different fard instead. By saying takbir with that intention, has he invalidated his first prayer? The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between intentional transfer (which invalidates) and unintentional mistakes (which allow repair). We will examine the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying takbir with the intention to leave the current prayer and start another. According to the Hanafi school, this invalidates the first prayer; it becomes fasid and cannot be continued.
The ruling applies to fard prayers; similar logic may apply to nafl, but the text focuses on fard.
2
Distinguish intentional vs. mistaken abandonment
If the person mistakenly gives salam (e.g., thinking the prayer is complete) and then realizes his error and says takbir to continue, he may do so. The first prayer is not invalidated because the mistake is common (umum balwa), and the school grants a concession.
The key factor is intent: deliberate transfer vs. unintentional error.
3
Examine the primary dalil
The text cites the hadith of Mu'adh: a man left the congregation and prayed alone, and the Prophet condemned him as a hypocrite. This shows that leaving a prayer deliberately invalidates it. The hadith of Dhul-Yadain supports the exception: the Prophet mistakenly gave salam and then continued, establishing the principle of building (bina) after a mistake.
Both hadith are from authoritative sources (Abu Dawud, Bukhari) and are considered zanni al-thubut.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Given a scenario, determine whether the first prayer is invalid or can be continued. Consider the presence of intent and whether the action was a common mistake.
For example, if someone in Zuhr prayer thinks he should pray Asr instead and says takbir for Asr, Zuhr is invalid. If he mistakenly says salam after two rak'ah and then says takbir, he may continue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۳۸) والتكبير بنية الانتقال لصلوة أخرى غير صلوته

ترجمه : (۵۳۸) ایک نماز سے دوسری نماز کی طرف انتقال کی نیت سے تکبیر کہنا۔

تشریح : فرض نماز پڑھ رہا تھا اچانک خیال آیا کہ میں دوسرے وقت کا فرض پڑھ لوں اور اس ارادے سے اس نماز سے نکل کر دوسری نماز کی تکبیر کہہ لی تو پہلی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، اب اس پر بنا نہیں کرسکتا۔ کیونکہ پہلی نماز کو توڑ چکا ہے، ہاں نماز پڑھ رہا تھا اور بھول سے سلام پھیر لیا اور پھر خیال آیا کہ ابھی پہلی نماز پوری نہیں ہوئی ہے اس لئے دوبارہ تکبیر کہ لی تو پہلی نماز پر بنا کرنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ یہ عموم بلوی ہے۔

وجه : (۱) کیونکہ اسکو چھوڑ کر دوسری نماز شروع کردی تو دوسری نماز میں داخل ہونا اس وقت شمار کیا جائے گا جب پہلی نماز سے نکل اسکوچھوڑ تو کیا جائے، اسلئے پہلی نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں اسکا اشارہ موجود ہے. كان معاذ يصلى مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم يرجع فيؤمنا .... ثم جاء يؤم قومه فقرأ البقرة ، فاعتزل رجل من القوم فصلي، فقيل نافقت يا فلان ! ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب تخفیف الصلوۃ ، ص ۱۲۳، نمبر ۷۹۰) اس حدیث میں ایک صحابی نماز سے نکل گئے ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آدمی نماز سے بالکل نکل جائے تو وہ نماز باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ (۳) اور پہلی نماز میں بھول کر سلام پھیر دیا اور دوبارہ بنا کرنا چاہتا ہے تو کر سکتا ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم انصرف من اثنتين ، فقال له ذو اليدين : أقصرت الصلوة أم نسيت يا رسول الله ؟ فقال رسول الله : أصدق ذو اليدين ؟ فقال الناس : نعم ، فقام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فصلى اثنتين أخريين ، ثم سلم ، ثم كبر، فسجد مثل سجوده أو اطول ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب ھل یا خذ الامام اذ اشک بقول الناس؟ ، ص ۹۹ نمبر ۷۱۴ را بود او د شریف، باب السهو فی السجدتین ، ص۱۵۳، نمبر ۱۰۰۸) اس حدیث میں اسی نماز کو دوبارہ شروع فرمایا تو پہلی نماز باقی رہی ۔۔ درمیان نماز میں بات کی اس سے نماز ٹوٹی یا نہیں اسکی بحث پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
(538) And the takbir with the intention of transferring to another prayer other than his prayer.

Translation: (538) Saying takbir with the intention of moving from one prayer to another.

Commentary: He was praying a fard prayer, suddenly thought to pray the fard of another time, and with that intention left the current prayer and said takbir for the other prayer—then the first prayer becomes invalid, and he cannot build upon it. However, if he was praying and mistakenly said the salam, then realized the prayer was not complete and said takbir again, it is permissible to build upon the first prayer because it is a common occurrence (umum balwa).

Evidence: (1) Leaving the first prayer and starting another indicates that the first is abandoned and becomes invalid. (2) Hadith of Mu'adh: he prayed with the Prophet, then returned to lead his people and recited al-Baqarah; a man left the congregation and prayed alone, and was criticized as a hypocrite—this shows leaving a prayer invalidates it. (3) Hadith of Dhul-Yadain: the Prophet mistakenly gave salam after two rak'ahs, then completed the prayer with two more rak'ahs and did sujood as-sahw—this shows that if the mistake is common, one can continue building.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about intentionally transferring from one prayer to another by saying takbir. The Hanafi position: if someone, while in a fard prayer, intends to pray a different fard (e.g., the missed one) and says takbir to start that new prayer, the first prayer becomes invalid and cannot be resumed. However, if he mistakenly said salam before completing the prayer, then realized and said takbir again, he may continue (bina) because it is a common occurrence (umum balwa). The evidence includes the hadith of Mu'adh (where a man left the congregation and prayed alone, which was condemned) and the hadith of Dhul-Yadain (where the Prophet continued after a mistaken salam). The distinction is based on intentional vs. mistaken abandonment.

Key Terms
بنية الانتقال (niyyat al-intiqal): The intention to transfer from one prayer to another, which invalidates the current prayer.
عموم بلوی (umum balwa): A widespread occurrence or common difficulty that provides a concession in the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person, while praying Zuhr, decides to pray Asr instead and says takbir for Asr?
A) The Zuhr prayer becomes invalid and cannot be resumed.
B) The Zuhr prayer becomes nafl, and Asr is valid.
C) Both prayers are valid if he intended both.
D) He must repeat both prayers.

Key Takeaway
Intentional transfer invalidates the first prayer; accidental mistakes allow continuation due to umum balwa.

The Moment of Prayer Completion: After the Final Sitting
Ruling on when invalidating actions nullify the prayer relative to the final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether an invalidating action nullifies the prayer based on its timing relative to the final sitting of tashahhud.

Core Idea
The prayer is complete after sitting for tashahhud; invalidators after that do not break it.

In the previous lessons, we learned that certain actions invalidate the prayer (mufsidat). But what if such an action occurs near the end of the prayer? The Hanafi school clarifies that the prayer's completion hinges on the final sitting of tashahhud. This lesson will focus on that critical moment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the occurrence of any invalidating event (like hadath, laughter, etc.) during prayer. The ruling depends on the timing relative to the final sitting.
2
Locate the condition
The prayer is considered complete after sitting for the measure of tashahhud in the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah).
The measure of tashahhud is the time to recite at-tahiyyat.
3
Apply the condition
If the invalidator occurs after that sitting, the prayer is valid; if before, it is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۳۹) اذا حصلت هذه المذكورات قبل شيئاً لم يقرأه

ترجمه : (۵۳۹) یہ تمام مذکورات اخیر قعدہ میں مقدار تشہد سے اگر پہلے حاصل ہوں تو مفسد صلوۃ ہوں گے۔

تشریح : درمیان میں حدث ہونے کے تمام صورتیں تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد پیش آئیں تو نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اس سے پہلے پیش آئی تو نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی۔
(539) If these mentioned things occur before he has recited something [i.e., before the final sitting of tashahhud].

Translation: (539) All these mentioned things, if they occur in the final sitting before the measure of tashahhud, are invalidators of the prayer.

Commentary: If any of the invalidating events occur after sitting for the measure of tashahhud in the final sitting, the prayer is complete (valid). If they occur before that, the prayer breaks.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a concluding general ruling that applies to all the invalidating actions (mufsidat) mentioned earlier in the chapter. The rule: if any of these invalidating events (such as hadath, laughter, etc.) occur after the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) for the duration of the tashahhud, the prayer is complete and valid. If they occur before that, the prayer is invalid. This is because the final sitting with the tashahhud is the last essential part (rukn) of the prayer; after completing it, the prayer is effectively finished even if the salam has not been said yet.

Key Terms
قعدہ اخیر (qa'dah akhirah): The final sitting in prayer after the last sujood, in which the tashahhud is recited.
مقدار تشہد (miqdar al-tashahhud): The time it takes to recite the tashahhud (at-tahiyyat) in the final sitting.

D) He must perform sujood as-sahw.

Key Takeaway
An invalidator occurring after the final sitting of tashahhud does not break the prayer; the prayer is complete at that point.

When Takbir for Another Prayer Invalidates Salah
Ruling with proof on invalidation by intentional takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a prayer becomes invalid due to intentional takbir for another prayer and distinguish it from the case of forgetful salam.

Core Idea
Intentionally leaving a prayer by starting another invalidates it; forgetful exit does not.

Imagine you are in the middle of a fard prayer and suddenly think of praying another fard instead. If you say takbir with that intention, what happens to your current prayer? This passage clarifies that deliberate exit invalidates the first prayer, but forgetfully saying salam does not — due to the principle of umum balwa (widespread need). Understanding this distinction protects the validity of your salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying takbir with the intention to leave the current prayer and start another. The ruling: the first prayer becomes fasid (invalid) and cannot be continued.
Fasid means the prayer is void and must be repeated from the beginning.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Mu'adh (Sunan Abi Dawud) where a companion left the Prophet's congregation and prayed alone. The Prophet did not rebuke him for praying alone, indicating that by leaving the first prayer, it became invalid.
Also the hadith of Dhul-Yadain (Bukhari) is used to support the exception for forgetfulness.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the hadith of Mu'adh, the companion intentionally exited the Prophet's prayer to pray with his people. The absence of condemnation for praying alone shows that his first prayer was nullified, allowing a new prayer. Thus, intentional exit invalidates.
The companion's act is seen as a precedent that leaving one prayer to start another is permissible only if the first is invalid.
4
Note the exception (umum balwa)
If a person forgetfully says salam and then realizes the prayer is incomplete, they may repeat takbir and continue from where they left off. This is allowed because such forgetfulness is widespread (umum balwa), and hardship would result if the prayer were invalidated.
The hadith of Dhul-Yadain is used to support building upon the original prayer after forgetful salam.
5
Distinguish deliberate vs forgetful
Deliberate takbir for another prayer = first prayer invalid. Forgetful salam followed by immediate takbir to continue = first prayer valid, can be resumed. The key is intention: deliberate exit vs. accidental error.
This distinction is based on the principle that a prayer is only broken by a deliberate act of exit.

Source Text

Bab: What invalidates the prayer. (538) And saying takbir with the intention to transition to another prayer other than the one he is in. (539) When these mentioned things occur before... (hadith text). Translation: (538) Saying takbir with the intention of transitioning from one prayer to another. Explanation: He was praying fard, suddenly thought to pray another fard, and with that intention left this prayer and said takbir for another, then the first prayer becomes invalid. He cannot build upon it because he has broken the first prayer. Yes, if he was praying and forgetfully said salam, then remembered the prayer is not complete, so he repeats takbir, then building upon the first prayer is permissible because it is a widespread situation (umum balwa). Proof: (1) Because by leaving and starting another, entry into the second is counted only after exiting the first, so the first becomes void. (2) This hadith indicates: Mu'adh used to pray with the Prophet then go and lead his people... (hadith). (3) Hadith of Abu Hurairah about forgetfulness in prayer. (hadith).
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (hukm) from the chapter on nullifiers of prayer. The author states that if a person intentionally says takbir with the express intention of leaving his current prayer to begin another, the first prayer becomes invalid (fasid). The reasoning is that the takbir for the second prayer constitutes an intentional exit from the first, breaking continuity. However, if one forgetfully says salam and then realizes the prayer is incomplete, he may repeat the takbir and continue from where he left off, because this is a widespread need (umum balwa) and the prayer remains valid. The proofs include the hadith of Mu'adh where a companion left the congregation and prayed alone, indicating his first prayer was invalidated by leaving, and the hadith of Dhul-Yadain where the Prophet completed his prayer after forgetting, showing that building upon the original prayer is allowed when done due to forgetfulness.

Key Terms
عموم بلوى (umum balwa): A widespread need or situation that occurs frequently, making an exception acceptable in order to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Intentional exit from prayer by starting another invalidates the first; forgetful exit due to umum balwa allows resumption.

Invalidation by Event Before Final Sitting
Ruling on nullifiers before final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer when a nullifier occurs after the final tashahhud and identify the evidence (dalil) for this ruling.

Core Idea
After sitting for tashahhud, a hadath does not invalidate prayer; it is complete but deficient.

This lesson addresses a critical timing issue in prayer: what if a person breaks wudu after sitting for tashahhud but before salam? The Hanafi school considers the prayer complete because the obligatory acts are done. We will examine the evidence and the rational basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Event
The act is prayer. The event is a nullifier (e.g., hadath) occurring after the final sitting for tashahhud.
The final sitting means sitting for the duration of at least the tashahhud.
2
State the Ruling
The prayer is complete (sahih ma'a al-naqs) and does not need to be repeated.
It is deficient (naqs) because the salam and certain sunan were not performed, but it is valid.
3
Analyze the Dalil
The hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly states that after the imam sits and then has an event, his prayer is complete (tammat). This indicates that the final sitting fulfills the prayer's requirements.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Darqutni.
4
Understand the Principle
All the fara'id (obligatory acts) are completed before the final sitting. Only wajib (salam) and sunnah (durud, dua) remain, so the prayer is considered complete.
The principle 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applies: the main objective of prayer is fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۳۹) یہ تمام مذکورات اخیر قعدہ میں مقدار تشہد سے اگر پہلے حاصل ہوں تو مفسد صلوۃ ہوں گے۔ تشریح : درمیان میں حدث ہونے کے تمام صورتیں تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد پیش آئیں تو نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اس سے پہلے پیش آئی تو نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی۔
 ثمرة النجاح جلد ا باب ما يفسد الصلوة الجلوس الاخير مقدار التشهد . (۵۴۰) ويُفسدها ايضا مدُّ الهمزة فى التكبير ( ۵۴۱) وقراءة ما لا يحفظه من مصحف
وجه : (۱) کیونکہ فرائض تو سارے پورے ہو چکے ہیں اب صرف سلام باقی ہے جو واجب ہے، اور درود شریف پڑھنا اور دعا پڑھنا باقی ہے جو سنت ہیں اس لئے نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ (۲) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال اذا قضى الامام الصلوة وقعد فاحدث قبل ان يتكلم فقد تمت صلوته ومن كان خلفه ممن اتم الصلوة (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الامام مسحدث بعد یا برفع رأسه، ص ۹۸، نمبر ۶۱۷ / ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل يحدث بعد التشهد ،ص۹۲، نمبر ۴۰۸ دار قطنی ، باب من احدث قبل التسليم في آخر صلوته او احدث قبل تسليم الامام فقد تمت صلوتی ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد حدث کر دیا تو نماز پوری ہو گئی اس لئے اسکی نماز نقص کے ساتھ پوری ہوگئی اسلئے دوبارہ نماز پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔(۳) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ ان رسول اللہ لا اخذ بيد عبد الله فعلمه التشهد في الصلوة فذكر مثل دعاء حديث الاعمش اذا قلت هذا او قضيت هذا فقد قضيت صلوتک ان شئت ان تقوم فقم وان شئت ان تقعد فاقعد ۔ ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب التشهد ، ص ۱۴۶، نمبر ۹۷۰) اس حدیث میں فرمایا گیا کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے یا پڑھنے کے بعد نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ اصول : تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد خلیفہ کے بجائے اصل پر قدرت ہوگئی تو چونکہ تمام فرائض پورے ہو چکے ہیں اس لئے نماز پوری ہوگئی کمی کے ساتھ ۔
Translation: (539) All these mentioned things, if they occur before the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud, are nullifiers of the prayer. Explanation: All forms of hadath (ritual impurity) during the prayer, if they occur after sitting for the amount of tashahhud, the prayer is complete. If before, the prayer is broken. Proof: (1) Because all the obligations (fara'id) are completed; only the salam remains which is wajib, and reciting the durud and dua are sunnah, so the prayer is complete. (2) Hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'When the Imam completes the prayer and sits, then has an event before speaking, his prayer is complete, and likewise those behind him who completed.' (Abu Dawud). (3) Hadith: The Prophet taught Abdullah the tashahhud saying: 'When you say this or complete this, your prayer is complete; if you wish to stand, stand; if you wish to sit, sit.' (Abu Dawud). Principle: After sitting for the amount of tashahhud, one has power over the original (asl) instead of the substitute (khalifah); since all fara'id are complete, the prayer is complete with deficiency.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage clarifies the critical timing for nullifiers in prayer. The author states that if any invalidating event (like hadath) occurs after the worshipper has sat for the duration of at least the tashahhud in the final sitting, the prayer is considered complete and valid, although deficient (naqs). If the event occurs before that sitting, the prayer is invalid. The reasoning is that all obligatory acts (fara'id) have been performed; only wajib and sunnah acts remain. The proofs are hadiths establishing that after the tashahhud, the prayer is deemed finished. The principle (asl) mentioned is: after the final sitting, one has direct control over the 'asl' (the complete prayer) rather than the substitute (the incomplete version), so the prayer is valid despite the event.

Key Terms
آخر قعدہ (akhir qa'dah): The final sitting in prayer after the last sajdah, in which tashahhud is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be restarted.
B) The prayer is complete and valid, though deficient.
C) The prayer is valid only if he repeats tashahhud.
D) The prayer becomes nafl.

Key Takeaway
After sitting for the amount of tashahhud, a hadath does not invalidate prayer; it is complete but deficient, and no repetition is required.

Invalidation by Lengthening Hamzah in Takbir
Ruling with implicit proof: mispronunciation changing meaning invalidates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the hamzah in 'Allahu Akbar' is lengthened to form a question and explain why the prayer becomes invalid.

Core Idea
Changing the meaning of takbir by lengthening the hamzah invalidates prayer because it alters the essential dhikr.

In this lesson, we examine a subtle invalidator of prayer: mispronouncing the opening takbir in a way that changes its meaning. The source passage from Thamaratun Najah teaches us that if one lengthens the initial hamzah of 'Allahu' so that it sounds like a question, the prayer becomes null. Understanding this ruling sharpens our awareness of the precision required in the acts of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The specific mispronunciation of the takbir: lengthening the hamzah in 'Allahu' such that it becomes a question.
2
Recognise the change in meaning
The original 'Allahu Akbar' means 'Allah is Great'. With lengthened hamzah, it becomes 'A-llahu Akbar?' meaning 'Is Allah greater?'
This changes a statement of praise into a question.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
Any alteration that changes the meaning of an essential dhikr in prayer invalidates the prayer.
The takbir is an essential component (rukn).
4
State the ruling
The prayer becomes fasid (invalid) and must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۴۰) اللہ اکبر کوالف ممدودہ سے پڑھنا۔ تشريح : اللہ اکبر، میں اللہ کے شروع کے الف کو کھینچے گا تو اللہ اکبر ، ہو جائے گا اور ترجمہ ہوگا کیا اللہ بڑا ہے، اس لئے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
ترجمه : (۵۴۱) بغیر یاد کے قرآن مجید کو دیکھ کر پڑھنا۔ تشریح : اگر قرآن یاد ہے اور اس کو دیکھ کر نماز میں پڑھ رہا ہے تو یہ ممکن ہے کہ یادداشت سے پڑھ رہا ہو قرآن کریم ویسے ہی کھلا رکھا ہو اس لئے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی لیکن اگر یاد نہیں ہے اور قرآن کو دیکھ کر اس سے پڑھ رہا ہے تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : اسکی دو وجہ بیان فرماتے ہیں (۱) ایک وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن سے پڑھنا اس سے تلقین کرنا ہے، یعنی اس سے لقمہ لینا ہے اور اس سے تعلیم اور تعلم کرنا ہے، اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اپنے مقتدی کے علاوہ سے لقمہ لینا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عـن عـلـى قـال قال رسول الله عل الله : يا على ! لا تفتح على الامام في الصلوة - (ابوداود شریف، باب النھی عن التلقین ،ص ۱۳۹، نمبر ۹۰۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت نہ ہو تو لقمہ نہیں دینا چاہئے ۔ (۲) أن علـيـا قال : لا تفتح على الامام قوم و
Translation: (540) Reciting 'Allahu Akbar' with a lengthened alif. Explanation: In 'Allahu Akbar', if one lengthens the initial alif of 'Allahu', it becomes 'A-llahu Akbar?' meaning 'Is Allah greater?', so the prayer becomes invalid. Translation: (541) Reciting from the mushaf (copy of the Quran) what one does not memorise. Explanation: If one has memorised and recites while looking at the mushaf, it is possible he is reciting from memory, so the prayer is not invalid. But if he does not memorise and recites by looking at the mushaf, the prayer becomes invalid. Proof: Two reasons: (1) Reciting from the mushaf involves receiving prompts (talqin) from it, which is like learning and teaching, and it has passed that receiving talqin from other than one's own follower is not permissible. Hadith: 'O Ali, do not prompt the imam in prayer.' (Abu Dawud). (2) Ali said: 'Do not prompt the imam...' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings on invalidators of prayer. First (540): If one lengthens the hamzah in 'Allahu' so that it becomes a question ('A-llahu?'), the meaning changes and the takbir becomes invalid; thus the prayer is nullified. Second (541): Reciting directly from a mushaf (physical copy of the Quran) while relying on it for the text invalidates the prayer if the reciter does not have the verses memorized. If he is merely looking but reciting from memory, it is not invalid. The proof cites the hadith prohibiting prompting (talqin) the imam, as reading from a mushaf entails taking prompt from the text, which is akin to learning and teaching within prayer – an invalidating act. The text ends abruptly; the second proof is incomplete.

Key Terms
مد الهمزة (madd al-hamzah): Lengthening the hamzah in 'Allahu' so that it becomes a question (astifham), changing the meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The prayer becomes invalid (fasid) because the meaning changed.
C) The prayer is valid if the person did not intend to change the meaning.
D) The prayer becomes makruh but not invalid.

Key Takeaway
Lengthening the hamzah in 'Allahu' to form a question invalidates the prayer because it changes the essential meaning of the takbir.

Invalidation by Reciting from Mushaf without Memorisation
Ruling with explicit proof: hadith on talqin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ruling on reciting from a mushaf during prayer and explain the evidence from the hadith on talqin.

Core Idea
Reciting from a mushaf without memorization invalidates prayer because it relies on external prompting, which is prohibited.

The second invalidator discussed in the source passage concerns reciting the Quran directly from a physical copy (mushaf) while relying on it for the text. The Hanafi school distinguishes between reciting from memory while the mushaf is open (permissible) and reading directly from it without memorization (invalid). The proof comes from the hadith prohibiting talqin (prompting) in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Reciting Quran from a mushaf (physical copy) during salah while relying on it for the text.
2
Check the condition of memorisation
Determine whether the reciter has memorised the verses being recited.
If memorised, looking at the mushaf is permissible as it is for reference only.
3
Understand the concept of talqin
Talqin means prompting or receiving words from an outside source. Reading from a mushaf without memorisation is considered talqin.
4
Apply the hadith evidence
The hadith 'O Ali, do not prompt the imam in prayer' (Abu Dawud) prohibits receiving guidance from others; similarly, the mushaf provides guidance.
5
Conclude the ruling
If not memorised, the prayer becomes fasid (invalid) due to prohibited talqin.

Source Text

Last Sitting Completes the Prayer
Ruling with proof: prayer completes after tashahhud sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prayer is completed after the last sitting for tashahhud and explain the proofs and the concept of deficiency (naqs).

Core Idea
Prayer is complete after tashahhud sitting; later events do not invalidate.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling: if a person sits in the final sitting for the duration of tashahhud and then something occurs that normally invalidates prayer, the prayer remains valid. The author clarifies that this is because all obligatory acts are done; only the salutation (wajib) and sunnah acts remain. Two hadiths establish this, and a legal principle reinforces it. Understanding this helps you distinguish between completion and perfection in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the legal status of a prayer if the person breaks wudu after the last sitting for tashahhud? The passage states the prayer is complete (sahih) but with deficiency.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why is it complete? Because all fara'id are done; only wajib (salam) and sunnah remain. In Hanafi fiqh, missing a wajib does not invalidate the prayer.
3
Examine the first hadith proof
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'When the imam completes the prayer and sits, then has an event before speaking, his prayer is complete.' This directly supports the ruling.
4
Examine the second hadith proof
The hadith teaching tashahhud: 'When you say this, you have completed your prayer.' This shows that tashahhud marks completion.
5
Apply the principle
After sitting for tashahhud, one has power over the original (qiyam) instead of the substitute (qu'ud), so the obligation is fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلوة الجلوس الاخير مقدار التشهد . (۵۴۰) وجه : (۱) کیونکہ فرائض تو سارے پورے ہو چکے ہیں اب صرف سلام باقی ہے جو واجب ہے، اور درود شریف پڑھنا اور دعا پڑھنا باقی ہے جو سنت ہیں اس لئے نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ (۲) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال اذا قضى الامام الصلوة وقعد فاحدث قبل ان يتكلم فقد تمت صلوته ومن كان خلفه ممن اتم الصلوة (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الامام مسحدث بعد یا برفع رأسه، ص ۹۸، نمبر ۶۱۷ / ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل يحدث بعد التشهد ،ص۹۲، نمبر ۴۰۸ دار قطنی ، باب من احدث قبل التسليم في آخر صلوته او احدث قبل تسليم الامام فقد تمت صلوتی ص ۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد حدث کر دیا تو نماز پوری ہو گئی اس لئے اسکی نماز نقص کے ساتھ پوری ہوگئی اسلئے دوبارہ نماز پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔(۳) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ ان رسول اللہ لا اخذ بيد عبد الله فعلمه التشهد في الصلوة فذكر مثل دعاء حديث الاعمش اذا قلت هذا او قضيت هذا فقد قضيت صلوتک ان شئت ان تقوم فقم وان شئت ان تقعد فاقعد ۔ ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب التشهد ، ص ۱۴۶، نمبر ۹۷۰) اس حدیث میں فرمایا گیا کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے یا پڑھنے کے بعد نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ اصول : تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد خلیفہ کے بجائے اصل پر قدرت ہوگئی تو چونکہ تمام فرائض پورے ہو چکے ہیں اس لئے نماز پوری ہوگئی کمی کے ساتھ ۔
Chapter on what invalidates prayer. The last sitting to the extent of tashahhud. (540) Reason: (1) Because all obligations are complete, only salutation remains which is wajib, and reciting salawat and supplications remain which are sunnah, so the prayer will be complete. (2) The hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'When the imam completes the prayer and sits, then has an event before speaking, his prayer is complete, and whoever is behind him from those who completed the prayer.' (Abu Dawud, chapter of the imam having an event after raising his head, p. 98, no. 617; Tirmidhi, chapter of what is reported about the man who has an event after tashahhud, p. 92, no. 408; Daraqutni, chapter of who has an event before the salutation at the end of his prayer or before the imam's salutation, his prayer is complete, p. 368, no. 1407) From this hadith it is known that after sitting to the extent of tashahhud, if one has an event, the prayer is complete, so his prayer is complete with deficiency, so there is no need to repeat it. (3) This hadith: He took the hand of Abdullah and taught him tashahhud in prayer, then mentioned similar to the supplication of the hadith of A'mash: 'When you say this or complete this, you have completed your prayer; if you want to stand then stand, and if you want to sit then sit.' (Abu Dawud, chapter of tashahhud, p. 146, no. 970) In this hadith it is said that after sitting or reciting to the extent of tashahhud, the prayer is complete. Principle: After sitting to the extent of tashahhud, one has power over the original instead of the substitute, and since all obligations are complete, the prayer is complete with deficiency.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the validity of prayer after the last sitting. The author states that if a person sits in the final sitting for the duration of the tashahhud (the recitation of 'At-tahiyyat') and then something occurs that normally invalidates prayer (like breaking wudu), the prayer is still valid and does not need to be repeated. The reasoning is that all the obligatory acts (farā'id) have been completed; only the salutation (salam) remains, which is wajib (obligatory but not fard), and the recitation of durud and supplications are sunnah. Thus, the prayer is valid albeit with deficiency. The author then provides two hadith proofs. The first hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar states that if an imam completes the prayer and sits, then has an event before speaking, his prayer is complete. The second hadith teaches that after reciting tashahhud, one has effectively completed the prayer. The passage concludes with a legal principle (usul): after sitting for tashahhud, one has access to the original obligation (qiyām) instead of the substitute (qu'ūd), so the prayer is complete with deficiency.

Key Terms
تشہد (tashahhud): The recitation of 'At-tahiyyat' in the last sitting of prayer.
قاعدہ (qa'idah): The last sitting in prayer.
نقص (naqs): Deficiency; the prayer is valid but incomplete in perfection due to missing wajib or sunnah acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar cited in this lesson, when does the imam's prayer become complete after an event?
A) After he says the salutation.
B) After he sits and then has an event before speaking.
C) After he completes the entire prayer including sunnah.
D) Only if the event is unintentional.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the prayer is considered complete after the last sitting for tashahhud, and any subsequent invalidating event does not nullify it; the prayer remains valid, albeit with deficiency, and need not be repeated.

Elongating the Hamza in Takbir: When Pronunciation Invalidates Prayer
States that elongating the hamza in takbir invalidates prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the hamza in 'Allahu Akbar' is elongated and explain why it invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
If the takbir's meaning changes, prayer becomes invalid — even a vowel stretch matters.

In Salah, every word of the takbir carries weight. The Hanafi school emphasizes that even a subtle pronunciation change, like stretching the hamza in 'Allah', can alter the meaning from a declaration to a question. This lesson clarifies why such an error makes the prayer invalid (fasid) and what other analogous mistakes imply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is reciting the opening takbir ('Allahu Akbar') during Salah. This is a mandatory component (rukn) of the prayer.
The takbir must be pronounced correctly for the prayer to be valid.
2
Recognize the specific pronunciation error
The error is elongating the hamza at the beginning of 'Allah', resulting in 'Allaah' (with a stretched 'a' sound).
This is a common mistake; the hamza is a glottal stop that should be pronounced short.
3
Understand the semantic change
The elongated 'Allaah' changes the word from the name 'Allah' to an interrogative form meaning 'Is God?'. Thus the phrase 'Allaahu Akbar' becomes 'Is God great?' instead of 'God is great'.
The meaning shifts from an affirmation to a question, which is not the intended declaration of takbir.
4
Apply the ruling
According to the Hanafi school, any change in the wording of the takbir that alters its intended meaning invalidates the prayer. Therefore, such a mispronunciation makes the prayer fasid (invalid).
The ruling applies whether done intentionally or out of ignorance; the prayer must be repeated.
5
Distinguish from other pronunciation errors
Not all pronunciation mistakes invalidate prayer. Only those that change the meaning of an essential part (like takbir) or that are clearly deliberate and substantial are problematic.
Minor mistakes that do not alter meaning (e.g., slight intonation) are forgiven.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۴۰) اللہ اکبر کوالف ممدودہ سے پڑھنا۔ تشريح : اللہ اکبر، میں اللہ کے شروع کے الف کو کھینچے گا تو اللہ اکبر ، ہو جائے گا اور ترجمہ ہوگا کیا اللہ بڑا ہے، اس لئے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
Translation: (540) Reciting the takbir with a lengthened hamza. Explanation: In 'Allahu Akbar', if one stretches the initial hamza of 'Allah', it becomes 'Allaah', and the meaning becomes 'Is Allah great?', therefore the prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement about an invalidator of prayer. The author explains that if a person intentionally elongates the hamza in the takbir (saying 'Allaah' instead of 'Allah'), the meaning changes from a declaration of greatness to a question ('Is Allah great?'). This changes the intended meaning of the takbir, which is a fundamental part of prayer, thus invalidating the prayer. The ruling is straightforward: the prayer is fasid (invalid).

Key Terms
مد الهمزة (madd al-hamzah): Elongating the hamza sound in the takbir.
فاسد (fasid): Invalid; the prayer is not valid and must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it changes the meaning to a question.
C) Because it is not allowed in any recitation.
D) Because it shows disrespect.

Key Takeaway
Elongating the hamza in the takbir changes its meaning from an affirmation to a question, rendering the prayer invalid (fasid) in the Hanafi school.

Reciting from Mushaf Without Memorization Invalidates Prayer
Ruling that reciting from the Quran without memorization invalidates prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting from a mushaf during prayer, explain the distinction between memorized and non-memorized recitation, and cite the proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
Reciting from the mushaf without memorization is akin to external speech and invalidates prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a crucial ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the effect of looking at a physical copy of the Quran during prayer. The key distinction lies in whether the reciter has memorized the verses. If he recites from memory while the mushaf is open, the prayer remains valid; but if he relies on reading without memorization, the prayer becomes invalid. The author supports this ruling with hadith prohibiting prompting (talqin) and directing those who cannot recite to use tasbih instead of reading from the mushaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting Quran from a mushaf during prayer. The ruling: if the verses are memorized, prayer is valid; if not, prayer is invalid.
2
Understand the rationale
The author explains that reading from mushaf without memory is like receiving talqin, which is akin to teaching/learning and thus external speech.
3
Locate the proofs
The author cites hadith: the prohibition of prompting the imam (Abu Dawud), the report from Ali (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq), and the two hadiths that direct the one who cannot recite to say tasbih instead (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud).
4
Examine the hadith's relevance
The hadith on prompting shows that receiving external recitation is akin to speech. The hadiths on tasbih indicate that if one cannot recite, he is not instructed to read from a mushaf, implying it is not permissible.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
WhatsApp, phones, tablets: if a person can recite from memory but opens an app for verification, it's valid; but if he reads directly without memorization, it's invalid.

ترجمه : (۵۴۱) بغیر یاد کے قرآن مجید کو دیکھ کر پڑھنا۔ تشریح : اگر قرآن یاد ہے اور اس کو دیکھ کر نماز میں پڑھ رہا ہے تو یہ ممکن ہے کہ یادداشت سے پڑھ رہا ہو قرآن کریم ویسے ہی کھلا رکھا ہو اس لئے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی لیکن اگر یاد نہیں ہے اور قرآن کو دیکھ کر اس سے پڑھ رہا ہے تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : اسکی دو وجہ بیان فرماتے ہیں (۱) ایک وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن سے پڑھنا اس سے تلقین کرنا ہے، یعنی اس سے لقمہ لینا ہے اور اس سے تعلیم اور تعلم کرنا ہے، اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ اپنے مقتدی کے علاوہ سے لقمہ لینا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عـن عـلـى قـال قال رسول الله عل الله : يا علي ! لا تفتح على الامام في الصلوة - (ابوداود شریف، باب النھی عن التلقین ،ص ۱۳۹، نمبر ۹۰۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ضرورت نہ ہو تو لقمہ نہیں دینا چاہئے ۔ (۲) أن علـيـا قال : لا تفتح على الامام قوم و (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب تلقینۃ الامام ، ج ثانی ، ص۹۲ نمبر (۲۸۲۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اپنے امام کے علاوہ کو لقمہ نہ دے کیونکہ وہ کلام کے درجے میں ہے، اور کلام سے نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے، اسلئے قرآن کو دیکھ کر قرآت کرنے سے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ (۳) عن رفاعة بن رافع أن رسول الله الله بينما هو جالس في المسجد يو ما ..... فان كان معک قرآن فاقرأ ، و الا فاحمد الله و كبره و هلله . (ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی وصف الصلوۃ ص ۶۶ نمبر ۳۰۲) (۴) عن عبد الله بن ابي أوفى قال : جاء رجل الى النبي الله فقال : اني لا أستطيع أن أخذمن القرآن شيئاً فعلمنى ما يجزئنى منه فقال : قل سبحان الله و الحمد لله (ابوداود شریف، باب ما یجزی الامی والا عجمی من القرآة بص ۱۲۸، نمبر ۸۳۲) ان دونوں حدیثوں میں ہے کہ قرآن زبانی یاد نہ ہو تو الحمدللہ پڑھو اور تکبیر وغیرہ کہہ کر نماز پوری کرو۔ یہاں آیت یاد نہ ہونے کی شکل میں تکبیر وغیرہ کہنے کے لئے کہا یہ نہیں کہا کہ قرآن دیکھ کر پڑھو جس سے معلوم ہوا قرآن دیکھ کر پڑھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
Translation: (541) Reciting from the noble Quran by looking without memorizing. Explanation: If one has memorized the Quran and looks at it while praying, it is possible he is reciting from memory, so the prayer is not invalid. But if he does not remember and recites by looking at it, the prayer is invalid. Reason: Two reasons are given: (1) Reciting from the Quran is like receiving prompting (talqin) from it, i.e., taking prompts, and it constitutes teaching and learning, and it has passed earlier that taking a prompt from someone other than one's own follower is not valid. The hadith: From Ali, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'O Ali! Do not open for the imam in prayer.' (Abu Dawud, chapter of prohibition of prompting, p. 139, no. 908) From this hadith it is known that if there is no need, one should not prompt. (2) Ali said: Do not open for a people other than your imam... (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter of prompting the imam, vol. 2, p. 92, no. 2824) In this report, it is that one should not prompt someone other than his own imam, because it amounts to speech, and speech invalidates prayer, so reciting by looking at the Quran invalidates prayer. (3) From Rifa'ah ibn Rafi' that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, while sitting in the mosque one day... 'If you have Quran with you, recite, otherwise say Alhamdulillah, Takbir, and Tahlil.' (Tirmidhi, chapter of description of prayer, p. 66, no. 302) (4) From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: A man came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and said: 'I cannot memorize anything from the Quran, so teach me what suffices.' He said: 'Say Subhanallah and Alhamdulillah...' (Abu Dawud, chapter of what suffices the illiterate and non-Arab, p. 128, no. 832) In both these hadiths, when one does not know Quran by heart, he is told to say Alhamdulillah and takbir etc. to complete the prayer. He is not told to recite by looking at the Quran, which shows that reciting by looking at the Quran is not permissible.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding reciting the Quran from a mushaf during prayer. The author distinguishes two scenarios: if the person has memorized the verses and looks at the mushaf while reciting from memory, the prayer is valid; if he has not memorized and reads directly from the mushaf, the prayer becomes invalid. The reasoning is that reading from the mushaf in the latter case is equivalent to receiving talqin (prompting) from the Quran, which is akin to taking a lesson or being taught, and this is classified as external speech (kalam), which invalidates prayer. The author cites several hadiths: the prohibition of prompting the imam, the report from Ali, and the hadiths that instruct those who cannot recite Quran to say tasbih and tahmid instead of reading from a mushaf. These proofs establish that reciting without memorization is impermissible.

Key Terms
تلقین (talqīn): Prompting someone in recitation; receiving cues from an external source.
مصحف (mushaf): Physical copy of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does reciting from the Quran by looking invalidate the prayer?
A) If the person has memorized the verses
B) If the person has not memorized the verses
C) Always
D) Only if the mushaf is moved

Key Takeaway
Reciting from a mushaf without memorization invalidates prayer because it is akin to external speech (talqin); but reciting from memory while looking at the mushaf is valid.

Performing a Pillar with Exposed Awrah or Impurity Invalidates Prayer
Ruling that performing a rukn while awrah exposed or with impurity invalidates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which prayer becomes invalid due to exposed awrah or impurity and apply the Hanafi ruling on immediacy.

Core Idea
Prayer is invalid if awrah or impurity persists for the duration of one rukn.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from Hanafi fiqh regarding the validity of prayer when the awrah becomes exposed or impurity is present. The passage clarifies that immediate rectification preserves the prayer, but delay of one rukn causes invalidity. Understanding this threshold helps ensure the integrity of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the events
What two factors can affect prayer validity according to the passage? Note that both exposure of awrah and presence of preventative impurity are considered.
These are the events that could invalidate if prolonged.
2
Understand the time threshold
How long must the condition last to invalidate the prayer? The passage specifies the duration of one rukn.
3
Define the smallest rukn
What is the reference for the duration? The smallest rukn is one sajdah, performed by saying Subhanallah three times.
4
Apply the ruling
When does immediate action save the prayer? If the awrah is covered or the impurity removed before completing one rukn, the prayer remains valid.
Immediate means within less than the time of one rukn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۴۲) کشف عورت یا نجاست مانعہ کے ساتھ ایک رکن ادا کرنا یا ادا کر نا ممکن ہو۔ تشریح : ستر عورت کھلا اور فورا ڈھانپ لیا تو نماز نہیں ٹوٹے گی ، اسی طرح اتنی نجاست لگی کہ اس سے نماز نہیں ہوسکتی ہے، لیکن فورا اس کو دور کر دیا تو نماز نہیں ٹوٹے گی لیکن اگر اتنی دیر ستر کھلا رہا، یا نجاست لگی رہی کہ اس میں ایک رکن ادا کر سکتا ہو تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔۔ ایک چھوٹا سا رکن سجدہ، تین مرتبہ سبحان اللہ کہنے سے ادا ہوتا ہے۔
Translation: (542) Performing a rukn or being able to perform it while the awrah is exposed or with impurity that prevents validity. Explanation: If the awrah is uncovered and immediately covered, the prayer does not break. Similarly, if there is impurity that prevents prayer, but it is removed immediately, the prayer does not break. However, if the awrah remained uncovered or the impurity remained for such a duration that one could perform one rukn, then the prayer becomes invalid. The smallest rukn (sajdah) is performed by saying Subhanallah three times.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This is a ruling statement about conditions that invalidate prayer. The author explains that if a person's awrah (parts to be covered) becomes exposed or if an impurity that prevents the validity of prayer (like najasah) is present, but they are covered/removed immediately (within the time of one small rukn), the prayer remains valid. However, if the exposure or impurity persists for the duration of one rukn (e.g., the time to perform a sajdah with three Subhanallahs), the prayer becomes invalid (fasid). The threshold is defined: the smallest rukn is one sajdah, which takes about the time of three Subhanallahs. This ruling helps define immediacy in rectifying such issues.

Key Terms
عورت (awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer, for men from navel to knees, for women all except face and hands.
نجاست مانعہ (najasah mani'ah): Impurity that prevents the validity of prayer, such as urine, blood, etc., beyond the exempted amount.
رکن (rukn): A fundamental part of prayer; here specifically the smallest rukn is one sajdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One rakah
B) One sajdah
C) One tashahhud
D) One Subhanallah

Key Takeaway
Prayer remains valid if awrah or impurity is rectified within the time of one sajdah; otherwise, it becomes fasid.

Muqtadi Preceding Imam in a Rukn Invalidates Prayer
Ruling with proof about follower preceding imam in a rukn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a follower preceding the imam in a rukn invalidates his prayer and explain the evidence from the three hadith cited.

Core Idea
Preceding the imam in a single rukn nullifies the follower's prayer.

The source passage addresses a critical rule of congregational prayer: the follower must synchronize with the imam. If the follower performs a complete rukn entirely before the imam, the prayer becomes invalid. The author provides three hadith as evidence. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the muqtadi performing a rukn (e.g., ruku') entirely before the imam begins that rukn. The ruling is that the muqtadi's prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
2
Examine the first proof: prohibition of departing before imam
The hadith from Anas (Abu Dawud) forbids the follower from departing from prayer before the imam. Preceding the imam in a rukn is a form of departing, thus invalidates.
This hadith warns against abandoning the imam's leadership.
3
Examine the second proof: warning about raising head before imam
The hadith from Abu Hurairah (Abu Dawud) threatens that raising the head before the imam could turn one's head into a donkey's head, indicating severe prohibition.
This emphasizes the gravity of preceding the imam.
4
Examine the third proof: command to follow imam
The well-known hadith (Bukhari, Muslim) states that the imam is appointed to be followed: when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise. Preceding contradicts following.
The command to follow implies the prohibition of preceding.
5
Synthesize the ruling and apply
The three hadith collectively establish that any complete rukn performed before the imam invalidates the follower's prayer. The ruling is absolute, regardless of intent.
The Hanafi school holds this as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۴۳) امام سے پہلے مقتدی کوئی رکن ادا کر لیوے کہ امام اس رکن میں اس کا شریک نہ ہو۔ تشریح : مثلا مقتدی نے امام سے پہلے رکوع کر لیا، اور امام کے رکوع میں جانے سے پہلے مقتدی نے سراٹھا لیا جسکی وجہ سے مقتدی امام کے ساتھ پورے رکن میں شریک نہیں رہا تو مقتدی کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن انس ان النبى الا الله محضهم على الصلاة و نهاهم ان ينصرفوا قبل انصرافه من الصلاة - ابوداود شریف، باب فیمن ینصرف قبل الامام، ص ۱۰۱، نمبر ۶۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام سے پہلے نماز سے نہ نکلے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله اما يخشى او الا يخشى احدكم اذا رفع رأسه و الامام ساجد ان يحول الله رأسه رأس حمار او صورته صورة حمار ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب التشديد فيمن يرفع قبل الامام او يضع قبلہ ،ص ۱۰۱، نمبر ۶۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام سے پہلے سر نہ اٹھائے ۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام کی متابعت کرو ۔ عن انس بن مالك ..... و قال انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به فاذا كبر فكبروا و اذا ركع فاركعوا و اذا رفع فارفعوا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب صلاة القاعد ، ص ۱۷۸، نمبر ۱۱۱۴ر مسلم شریف، باب ائتمام المأموم بالا مام، ص ۱۷۴ نمبر ۹۲۱/۴۱۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام کے ساتھ تکبیر کہو
Translation: (543) The muqtadi performs a rukn before the imam such that the imam does not share that rukn with him. Explanation: For example, the muqtadi bowed (ruku') before the imam, and before the imam went into ruku', the muqtadi raised his head, so the muqtadi did not share the entire rukn with the imam; then the muqtadi's prayer becomes invalid. Reason: (1) In this hadith: from Anas that the Prophet, peace be upon him, encouraged them on prayer and forbade them from departing before his departure from prayer. (Abu Dawud, chapter of one who departs before the imam, p. 101, no. 624) This hadith prohibits leaving the prayer before the imam. (2) From Abu Hurairah, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Does not fear, or will not one of you, when he raises his head while the imam is prostrating, that Allah will turn his head into a donkey's head or his form into a donkey's form?' (Abu Dawud, chapter of severity on one who raises before the imam or places before him, p. 101, no. 623) This hadith prohibits raising the head before the imam. (3) This hadith commands following the imam: from Anas ibn Malik, he said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; when he says takbir, say takbir; when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise.' (Bukhari, chapter of prayer of a sitting person, p. 178, no. 1114; Muslim, chapter of following the imam for the follower, p. 174, no. 921/411) This hadith commands saying takbir with the imam.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof about a muqtadi (follower) preceding the imam in a rukn (pillar of prayer). The author clarifies that if the muqtadi performs a rukn (e.g., ruku') before the imam and then lifts his head before the imam begins that rukn, the muqtadi has not shared the rukn with the imam. In such a case, the muqtadi's prayer becomes invalid (fasid). Three hadiths are cited: (1) The Prophet forbade departing from prayer before the imam. (2) He warned that raising the head before the imam is akin to having one's head turned into a donkey's head. (3) The well-known hadith that the imam is to be followed in every action. These proofs establish that preceding the imam invalidates the follower's prayer.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadī): The person praying behind the imam (follower).
مسابقت (musābaqat): Preceding the imam in an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The follower's prayer is invalid
C) The prayer is valid but makruh
D) The follower should wait and repeat later

Key Takeaway
Preceding the imam in a complete rukn invalidates the follower's prayer, based on the command to follow the imam.

Invalidation by Uncovering Awrah or Impurity for a Pillar
Lists invalidation of prayer by uncovered awrah or impurity lasting a pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on uncovering awrah or having impurity during prayer, and apply the Hanafi rule that the prayer remains valid only if covered or removed immediately, but becomes invalid if it persists for the time of one pillar.

Core Idea
Prayer is invalid only if awrah or impurity persists for one full pillar; immediate rectification preserves validity.

This lesson clarifies a specific point from the chapter on things that invalidate prayer. The Hanafi school teaches that if a person's 'awrah becomes uncovered or they have a preventing impurity on their body or clothes, the prayer is not automatically invalidated. Instead, the key is the duration: if the uncovered state or impurity remains for the length of time it takes to perform one pillar of prayer (the smallest being prostration with three tasbihat), the prayer becomes batil. If it is covered or removed immediately, the prayer remains valid. This ruling reflects the school's practical leniency while emphasizing the importance of covering and purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the potential invalidator
The act is prayer (salah). The potential invalidators are: (1) uncovering the 'awrah, and (2) having a preventing impurity (najasah mani'ah) on the body, clothes, or place of prayer.
Preventing impurity means impurity that would prevent the prayer from being valid if present; minor impurities that are excused do not count.
2
Understand the time threshold
The prayer becomes invalid (batil) only if the uncovered state or the impurity remains for the duration of one pillar. The smallest pillar in prayer is prostration (sajdah), which is considered to be performed by saying 'Subhan Allah' three times.
If the condition lasts less than that (i.e., immediate correction), the prayer is valid.
3
Apply the exception of immediate rectification
If the person covers the 'awrah or removes the impurity immediately (within the time of less than one pillar), the prayer remains valid. This shows the Hanafi emphasis on intentionality and minimal disruption.
Immediate means without significant delay; the exact measure is the time to say 'Subhan Allah' thrice.
4
Distinguish from other invalidators
This ruling is specific to uncovering and impurity. Other actions, such as speaking intentionally, laughing aloud, or turning away from the qiblah, invalidate the prayer immediately regardless of duration.
The measure of one pillar is unique to these two invalidators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلوة (۵۴۲) واداء ركن او امكانه مع كشف العورة او مع نجاسة مانعة . ترجمه : (۵۴۲) کشف عورت یا نجاست مانعہ کے ساتھ ایک رکن ادا کرنا یا ادا کر نا ممکن ہو۔ تشریح : ستر عورت کھلا اور فورا ڈھانپ لیا تو نماز نہیں ٹوٹے گی ، اسی طرح اتنی نجاست لگی کہ اس سے نماز نہیں ہوسکتی ہے، لیکن فورا اس کو دور کر دیا تو نماز نہیں ٹوٹے گی لیکن اگر اتنی دیر ستر کھلا رہا، یا نجاست لگی رہی کہ اس میں ایک رکن ادا کر سکتا ہو تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔۔ ایک چھوٹا سا رکن سجدہ، تین مرتبہ سبحان اللہ کہنے سے ادا ہوتا ہے۔
Chapter: What invalidates prayer. (542) And performing a pillar, or the possibility of it, while the 'awrah is uncovered or with a preventing impurity. Translation: (542) Performing a pillar or making it possible with uncovering of the 'awrah or with a preventing impurity. Explanation: If the 'awrah is uncovered and covered immediately, the prayer is not invalidated. Similarly, if so much impurity is present that prayer is not valid without it, but it is removed immediately, the prayer is not invalidated. However, if the 'awrah remains uncovered or the impurity remains for such a duration that one could perform one pillar, then the prayer becomes invalidated. A small pillar, like prostration, is performed by saying 'Subhan Allah' three times.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on what invalidates prayer. It explains that if a person's 'awrah becomes uncovered or they have a preventing impurity on their body or clothes, but they cover it or remove it immediately (within the time it takes to perform one small pillar, e.g., saying Subhan Allah three times), the prayer remains valid. However, if it remains for the duration of a full pillar, the prayer becomes invalid. The smallest pillar in prayer is considered the prostration, which can be completed by glorifying Allah thrice. This ruling emphasizes the importance of maintaining purity and covering during prayer, but also shows the Hanafi leniency for immediate rectification.

Key Terms
كشف العورة (kashf al-'awrah): Uncovering the parts of the body that must be concealed during prayer.
نجاسة مانعة (najasah mani'ah): Impurity that prevents the validity of prayer if present on body, clothes, or place.
ركن (rukn): A fundamental component of prayer; its omission invalidates prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any uncovered 'awrah, even if covered immediately.
B) Uncovered 'awrah that remains for the duration of one pillar.
C) Uncovered 'awrah that remains for two pillars.
D) Uncovered 'awrah only if not covered until after prayer.

Key Takeaway
Prayer remains valid if 'awrah or impurity is corrected immediately; it becomes invalid if the condition persists for one complete pillar.

Invalidation by Preceding the Imam in a Pillar
States the invalidation of follower's prayer if he performs a pillar before the imam and does not rejoin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a follower precedes the imam in a pillar and explain the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Preceding the imam in any pillar invalidates the follower's prayer.

In congregational prayer, following the imam is obligatory. Performing any pillar before the imam and not catching up violates this obligation, rendering the prayer invalid. This lesson examines the ruling and its basis in the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the follower performing a pillar (e.g., ruku, sujud) before the imam, and the ruling is that it invalidates the prayer.
2
Locate the hadith proofs
Three hadith are cited: prohibition of leaving before imam, warning against raising head before imam, and command to follow imam.
3
Trace the logical connection
The imperative to follow implies prohibition of preceding; violation of a wajib leads to invalidation if the follower does not rejoin.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools treat preceding as makruh but not invalid; Hanafi holds it as invalid due to the strong evidence.

Source Text
