(543) And the follower preceding the imam in a pillar while he is reciting, for it is speech. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq ...) In this narration, don't prompt anyone other than your imam because it is considered speech, and speech invalidates prayer. Therefore, reciting the Qur'an by looking at it invalidates prayer. (3) From Rifa'ah ibn Rafi' that the Messenger of Allah ... said: 'If you have some Qur'an with you, recite; otherwise, praise Allah, glorify Him, and declare His oneness.' (4) From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: A man came to the Prophet and said: 'I cannot learn anything of the Qur'an; teach me what suffices me.' He said: 'Say Subhan Allah and Alhamdulillah.' These two hadith show that if one does not memorize the Qur'an, he should recite Alhamdulillah and takbir etc. and complete the prayer. It was not said to recite by looking at the Qur'an, which indicates that reciting by looking is not permissible. Translation: (543) The follower should not perform any pillar before the imam such that the imam is not a partner with him in that pillar. Explanation: For example, the follower bowed before the imam, and before the imam bowed, the follower raised his head, so the follower was not a partner with the imam in the entire pillar; then the follower's prayer becomes invalid. Proof: (1) The hadith from Anas that the Prophet instructed them to stay in prayer and forbade them from leaving before his departure. (Abo Dawood) This hadith prohibits leaving before the imam. (2) From Abu Hurairah: The Prophet said: 'Does not one of you fear, when he raises his head while the imam is prostrating, that Allah will turn his head into a donkey's head or his face into a donkey's face?' (Abo Dawood) This forbids raising the head before the imam. (3) The hadith: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; when he says takbir, say takbir; when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise.' (Bukhari, Muslim) This commands following the imam.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that a follower (muqtadi) who performs a pillar (like bowing) before the imam and does not rejoin him in that pillar invalidates his prayer. The reason is that the follower must be in conformity with the imam. The text cites three hadith as evidence: the first prohibition of leaving before the imam, the second warning against raising the head before the imam, and the third commanding to follow the imam in all actions. The initial part also mentions that reciting Quran by looking at it is invalid because it is akin to speech. This is because looking at the Quran in prayer is considered taking help from outside, which is like speaking to someone. The core teaching is that any action that deviates from following the imam, especially preceding him, invalidates the follower's prayer.

Key Terms
مسابقة المقتدى (musabaqat al-muqtadi): The follower's act of performing a pillar before the imam.
ركن (rukn): A pillar of prayer; here refers to actions like ruku, sujud, etc.
كلام (kalam): Speech that is not part of the prayer; deliberately speaking invalidates prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a follower bows (ruku) before the imam and raises his head before the imam bows, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid.
B) The prayer is invalid.
C) The follower must perform sajdah sahw.
D) The follower must repeat the bowing after the imam.

Key Takeaway
Preceding the imam in a pillar without catching up invalidates the follower's prayer, based on the obligation to follow the imam as per the Sunnah.

Masbuq Following Imam in Sajdat al-Sahw After Separation
Ruling on the timing of masbuq's following imam in sajdat al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a masbuq (latecomer) following the imam in sajdat al-sahw and identify the critical condition (timing) that determines validity or invalidity.

Core Idea
A masbuq's prayer becomes invalid if he follows the imam in sajdat al-sahw after performing his own missed sajdah.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in congregational prayer. The masbuq (latecomer) must know exactly when he is still bound to follow the imam and when he becomes independent. Misunderstanding this timing can render his prayer void. The ruling hinges on a single act: performing the prostration of the missed rak'ah severs the imam-follower relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the masbuq following the imam in sajdat al-sahw after the imam has made salam. The ruling depends on whether the masbuq has performed his own missed sajdah or not.
The masbuq is a latecomer who completes his prayer after the imam finishes.
2
Distinguish the two timeframes
Scenario A: The masbuq follows the imam in sajdat al-sahw before performing his own missed sajdah. Scenario B: He follows after performing his own missed sajdah (i.e., after completing a full rak'ah).
The key act is the prostration of the missed rak'ah.
3
Apply the ruling to each scenario
In Scenario A, the prayer is valid (the masbuq is still a follower). In Scenario B, the prayer becomes invalid (batil) because the masbuq is now following a stranger (ajnabi).
Following a stranger in prayer invalidates it.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Once the masbuq performs his own sajdah, he severs his connection with the imam. The imam is no longer his imam, so following him is like following a non-imam, which is not allowed.
This highlights the importance of the imam-follower relationship in congregational prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۴۴) و متابعة الامام في سجود السهو للمسبوق . ترجمه : (۵۴۴) مسبوق سجدہ سہو میں امام کی متابعت کرلے۔ تشريح : اس عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ، امام نے سلام پھیر دیا اس کے بعد مسبوق اپنی باقی نماز پوری کرنے کے لئے اٹھا اور ایک رکعت کا سجدہ بھی کر لیا، جسکی وجہ سے مسبوق اب امام سے بالکل الگ ہو گیا، اس کے بعد امام کو سہو یاد آیا اور سجدہ سہو کیا اور اس مسبوق نے بھی امام کی اتباع کی تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ مسبوق کے سجدہ کرنے کے بعد امام اب اس کا امام نہیں رہا، اجنبی ہو گیا اس لئے اجنبی کی اقتداء کرنے کی وجہ سے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن انگلی رکعت کا سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے تک امام کی اتباع میں سجدہ سہو کیا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی ، کیونکہ یہ ابھی تک اس کا امام ہے۔
(544) And the masbuq follows the imam in sajdat al-sahw. Translation: (544) The masbuq should follow the imam in sajdat al-sahw. Explanation: The meaning of this phrase is that after the imam has made the final salam, the masbuq stands up to complete his remaining prayer and has performed the prostration of one rak'ah, thereby becoming completely separate from the imam. Then the imam recalls the need for sajdat al-sahw and performs it, and the masbuq also follows the imam. In this case, his prayer becomes invalid because after the masbuq performed his prostration, the imam is no longer his imam; he has become a stranger (ajnabi). Following a stranger invalidates prayer. However, if the masbuq follows the imam in sajdat al-sahw before performing the prostration of the missed rak'ah, the prayer is not invalid, because the imam is still his imam at that point.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario for a masbuq (one who joined late) during sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The ruling is that if the imam performs the final salam, then the masbuq stands up to complete his missed rak'ah and performs the sajdah of that rak'ah, he has severed his connection with the imam. If thereafter the imam performs sajdat al-sahw and the masbuq follows him (by imitating), his prayer becomes invalid because he is now following a person who is not his imam. But if the masbuq has not yet performed his own sajdah and is still in the state of being a follower (muqtadi), then following the imam in sajdat al-sahw is valid and required. The key is the timing: before performing the missed sajdah, the masbuq remains in the imam's congregation; after that, he is independent.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joined the congregational prayer late, after missing one or more rak'ahs.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
اجنبی (ajnabi): A stranger; in this context, a person who is not the imam for the masbuq anymore.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a masbuq's following of the imam in sajdat al-sahw become invalid?
A) When the imam forgets and performs it after salam.
B) When the masbuq has performed his own sajdah after the imam's salam.
C) When the imam does not make salam.
D) When the masbuq has not yet completed his missed rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
A masbuq must only follow the imam's sajdat al-sahw before performing his own missed sajdah; after that, he is independent and following invalidates his prayer.

Not Repeating Final Sitting After Missed Sajdah Salbiyyah
States ruling on final sitting repetition after missed prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a missed obligatory prostration is recalled during the final sitting and explain why the prayer becomes invalid if the final sitting is not repeated.

Core Idea
A missed obligatory prostration recalled in the final sitting must be followed by a repeated final sitting; otherwise the prayer is invalid.

You are in the final sitting of your prayer when you suddenly realise you missed a prostration in an earlier rak'ah. What do you do? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on whether you must repeat the final sitting after performing that missed prostration, and why the order matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario: a person is in the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and remembers that they omitted the obligatory prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) of a previous rak'ah.
2
State the ruling
If the person performs the missed prostration at that point and then says salam without repeating the final sitting, the prayer becomes invalid (batil).
3
Identify the reason
The reason is that the final sitting is an obligatory (wajib) act that must be performed at the very end of the prayer. By performing the prostration after the final sitting and not repeating it, the final sitting is omitted from its proper place, causing invalidity.
4
Understand the distinction
Note that 'sajdah salbiyyah' is the prostration that is part of the rak'ah itself, distinct from sajdat al-sahw (forgetfulness) and sajdat al-tilawah (recitation). This ruling applies specifically to a missed obligatory prostration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۴۵) وعدم اعادة الجلوس الاخير بعد اداء سجدة صلبيّة تذكرها بعد الجلوس . ترجمه : (۵۴۵) قعدہ آخیرہ کو نہ لوٹائے اس کے بعد کہ صلبی سجدہ ادا کیا جو قعدہ آخیرہ کے بعد یاد آیا۔ تشریح : قعدہ آخیرہ میں یاد آیا کہ کسی رکعت کا اصلی سجدہ باقی رہ گیا ہے، اس نے اصلی سجدہ کیا، اور دوبارہ قعدہ آخیرہ کئے بغیر سلام پھیر دیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی وجه : کیونکہ قعدہ آخیرہ بالکل آخیر میں ہونا چاہئے ، اور یہاں رکعت کا سجدہ آخیر میں ہو گیا اور اس کے بعد قعدہ نہیں کیا جو فرض ہے تو گویا کہ فرض چھوڑ دیا اس لئے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ لغت : سجدة صلبة : رکعت کا سجدہ ۔ دوسرا ہے سجدہ سہو، تیسرا ہے سجدہ تلاوت۔
(545) And not repeating the final sitting after performing a 'salbiyyah' prostration that was recalled after the sitting. Translation: (545) Do not repeat the final sitting after performing the obligatory prostration that was recalled after the final sitting. Explanation: While in the final sitting, one remembers that the obligatory prostration of a rak'ah was missed. He performs that obligatory prostration and then makes salam without repeating the final sitting. In such case, his prayer becomes invalid. Reason: Because the final sitting must be at the very end. Here the rak'ah's prostration occurred at the end, and after it he did not perform the final sitting, which is obligatory. Thus he left an obligatory act, invalidating the prayer. Lexicon: Sajdah salbiyyah: the prostration of a rak'ah. The second is sajdat al-sahw, the third is sajdat al-tilawah.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a person is in the final sitting (qa'dah akhir) of prayer and remembers that he omitted the obligatory prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) of a previous rak'ah. If he immediately performs that missed prostration and then says salam without repeating the final sitting, his prayer becomes invalid. The reason is that the final sitting must be the last part of the prayer. By performing the prostration after the final sitting, the order is disturbed, and skipping the second final sitting means an obligatory act is omitted. The passage also defines 'sajdah salbiyyah' as the prostration belonging to the rak'ah, distinguishing it from sajdat al-sahw and sajdat al-tilawah.

Key Terms
سجدة صلبيّة (sajdah salbiyyah): The obligatory prostration that is part of the rak'ah itself, distinct from prostration of forgetfulness or recitation.
الجلوس الاخير (al-julus al-akhir): The final sitting in prayer, during which the tashahhud is recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Prayer is valid, no compensation needed.
B) Prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) Prayer is valid but sajdat al-sahw is required.
D) Prayer is valid if he makes niyyah to repeat the sitting.

Key Takeaway
The final sitting must be the very last action of the prayer; performing a missed obligatory prostration after it requires repeating the sitting to avoid invalidity.

Pillar Performed While Asleep: Validity and Repeating
States that a pillar performed while asleep is invalid and must be repeated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a pillar performed while asleep and explain why it must be repeated upon waking.

Core Idea
A prayer action performed while asleep is void; consciousness is essential for valid prayer.

What happens if you perform part of your prayer while actually asleep? Does that action count? This lesson provides the Hanafi ruling: an action performed without awareness is not considered valid prayer. You must repeat that part after waking, or your entire prayer becomes invalid. This highlights the fundamental requirement of conscious intention in every pillar of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing a rukn (pillar) while asleep. The ruling: that action is not considered valid.
The passage explicitly states 'not counted' (la yu'tabar).
2
Determine the condition for validity
For a prayer action to be valid, the performer must be conscious and aware. Sleep nullifies awareness, so any action during sleep lacks the necessary intention (niyyah) and presence of mind.
This aligns with the broader principle that intention is required for every intentional act of worship.
3
Identify the consequence of omission after waking
If the person does not repeat that rukn after waking, the prayer is missing an obligatory component. Therefore, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
The ruling states the prayer becomes fasid (void).
4
Apply to a scenario
Example: A person is sleeping and, while still asleep, performs a sajdah (prostration). Upon waking, they do not repeat that sajdah. The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This scenario is directly covered by the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۴۶) و عدم اعادة ركن اداه نائما . ترجمه : (۵۴۶) نیند میں رکن ادا کئے ہوئے کا اعادہ نہ کرنا۔ تشریح : جور کن سوئے ہوئے میں ادا کیا اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، اس لئے بیدار ہونے کے بعد اس کو ادا نہیں کیا تو وہ فرض چھوڑ دیا اس لئے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
(546) And not repeating a pillar that he performed while asleep. Translation: (546) Not repeating a pillar performed in sleep. Explanation: The pillar that one performed while asleep is not considered valid. Therefore, if upon waking he does not repeat it, he has left an obligatory act, and his prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This ruling addresses the validity of actions performed while asleep during prayer. If a person is asleep (i.e., unconscious) and performs a pillar of prayer, that action is not considered valid because it lacks intention and awareness. Therefore, upon waking, that pillar must be performed properly. If it is not repeated, the prayer is incomplete and invalid. This highlights the importance of consciousness and intent for the validity of prayer actions.

Key Terms
نائما (na'iman): In a state of sleep; unconscious.
ركن (rukn): A pillar of prayer; an essential component without which the prayer is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid because sujud was physically performed.
B) The prayer is invalid.
C) The person must perform sajdat al-sahw.
D) The person must repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
A pillar performed while asleep is not valid and must be repeated upon waking; otherwise, the prayer becomes invalid.

Imam's Laughter or Hadath After Final Sitting: Effect on Masbuq
Ruling on imam's laughter/hadath after final sitting with masbuq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an imam laughs or intentionally breaks wudu after the final sitting with a masbuq, and explain why the masbuq's prayer is invalidated.

Core Idea
The masbuq's prayer is invalid if his imam becomes impure after the final sitting.

This passage clarifies a subtle point in congregational prayer: the effect of the imam's action on a latecomer (masbuq). While the imam's own prayer is complete and valid (though disliked) after the final sitting, his impairment invalidates the masbuq's prayer because the masbuq still relies on the imam's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The imam laughs audibly (qahqaha) or intentionally breaks wudu (hadath) after the final sitting while a masbuq is following.
2
Apply the general principle
Recall the rule: intentional hadath before final sitting invalidates prayer; after final sitting, prayer is valid but disliked (makruh tanzih).
3
Recognize the masbuq's situation
The masbuq has not completed his prayer; he still owes rak'ahs and is dependent on the imam's validity.
4
Determine the consequence for each
Imam's prayer is valid (makruh) because no obligation remains; masbuq's prayer becomes invalid because his imam is no longer in a valid state.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools do not distinguish between before and after the final sitting, treating any hadath as invalidating for all.

(۵۴۷) وقهقهة امام المسبوق وحدثه العمد بعد الجلوس الاخير . ترجمه : (۵۴۷) مسبوق کے امام کا قاعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد قہقہہ لگانا، یا جان کر حدث کرنا۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ سے پہلے جان کر حدث کر دیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ، اور قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد حدث کیا تو نماز کراہیت کے ساتھ پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ۔ قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد مسبوق کے امام نے قہقہ لگادیا یا جان کر حدث کر دیا تو اس کی نماز کراہیت کے ساتھ پوری ہو جائے گی کیونکہ اب کوئی فرض باقی نہیں رہا، لیکن مسبوق کی نماز ابھی بیچ میں ہے، اس کو ابھی ایک رکعت اور پڑھنی ہے اس لئے اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
(547) And the imam's laughter and his intentional hadath after the final sitting for the masbuq. Translation: (547) The imam of the masbuq laughing or intentionally breaking wudu after the final sitting. Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that if one intentionally breaks wudu before the final sitting, the prayer becomes invalid; but if after the final sitting, the prayer is completed with dislike. The scenario: After the final sitting, the imam laughs or intentionally breaks wudu. Then the imam's prayer is completed with dislike because no obligation remains, but the masbuq's prayer is still ongoing; he still has to perform one more rak'ah. Therefore, the masbuq's prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage explains the effect of the imam's laughter (laughter with sound) or intentional breaking of wudu (hadath) after the final sitting when there is a masbuq (latecomer) still praying. The general principle is that if a person breaks wudu intentionally before the final sitting, his prayer is invalid; if after the final sitting, the prayer is still valid but disliked (makruh) because no obligatory act remains. However, when there is a masbuq, the imam's prayer may be complete (since he finished his final sitting), but the masbuq's prayer is not yet complete; he still needs to stand up and perform a missed rak'ah. So if the imam laughs or breaks wudu intentionally after his own final sitting, the imam's prayer is valid (with dislike), but the masbuq's prayer becomes invalid because his imam is no longer in a state of purity or proper conduct to lead him. The masbuq must rely on the imam for the remainder of his prayer, and if the imam becomes invalid, the masbuq's prayer is invalidated.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Laughter with audible sound, which invalidates wudu and prayer in Hanafi fiqh.
حدث (hadath): The state of being without wudu; here, intentional breaking of wudu (e.g., passing wind, urination).
مسبوق (masbuq): A follower who joined late and still owes rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario described in this lesson, what is the ruling for the imam's prayer when he intentionally laughs after the final sitting?
A) Valid and not disliked
B) Valid but makruh tanzih
C) Invalid
D) Invalid only if the masbuq also laughs

Key Takeaway
The masbuq's prayer is invalid if the imam commits a hadath or laughs intentionally after the final sitting, because the masbuq's prayer remains dependent on the imam until completion.

Effect of Imam's Laughter or Hadath After Final Sitting on Masbuq
Ruling with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an imam's intentional hadath or loud laughter after the final sitting and determine its effect on the masbuq's prayer.

Core Idea
Imam's prayer completes with karahah; masbuq's prayer invalidates.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in congregational prayer: what happens when the imam, after completing the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah), intentionally breaks wudu (hadath) or laughs loudly (qahqaha). The ruling affects not only the imam but also the masbuq (latecomer) who still has a rak'ah left. The source passage provides the Hanafi position supported by hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key distinction
Recognize that the ruling depends on when the hadath occurs: before or after the final sitting. Before: prayer invalid. After: prayer completes with karahah.
The final sitting is the point where all fard acts are done.
2
Apply the distinction to the imam
If the imam laughs loudly or breaks wudu after the final sitting, his own prayer is considered complete (with karahah) because no fard remains.
Karahah means dislike; the prayer is valid but deficient.
3
Analyze the effect on the masbuq
The masbuq's prayer is still incomplete (he has one more rak'ah). Since the imam's prayer became invalid at the moment of hadath, the masbuq's link to the imam is severed, invalidating his prayer.
The masbuq must restart his prayer.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith from Darqutni states that the imam's prayer and the prayer of those who caught the beginning are complete. The opposite (mafhum mukhalaf) indicates that those who missed the beginning (masbuq) have invalid prayer.
Other hadith establish that hadath and qahqaha invalidate prayer and wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقهقهة امام المسبوق وحدثه العمد بعد الجلوس الاخير. ترجمه : (۵۴۷) مسبوق کے امام کا قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد قہقہہ لگانا، یا جان کر حدث کرنا۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ سے پہلے جان کر حدث کر دیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی، اور قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد حدث کیا تو نماز کراہیت کے ساتھ پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ۔ قعدہ اخیرہ کے بعد مسبوق کے امام نے قہقہ لگادیا یا جان کر حدث کر دیا تو اس کی نماز کراہیت کے ساتھ پوری ہو جائے گی کیونکہ اب کوئی فرض باقی نہیں رہا، لیکن مسبوق کی نماز ابھی بیچ میں ہے، اس کو ابھی ایک رکعت اور پڑھنی ہے اس لئے اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ (۱) اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ امام نے جب حدث کیا تو امام کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو گئی تھی لیکن تمام فرائض پورے ہو گئے تھے اسلئے دوبارہ بناء کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں رہی ، اسلئے نقص کے ساتھ نماز پوری سمجھ لی گئی۔ لیکن مسبوق کی نماز ابھی باقی ہے اور اسکے فرائض بھی باقی ہیں اور اسکے درمیان ہی میں امام نے حدث کر دیا تو حقیقت میں امام کی نماز فاسد ہونے کی وجہ سے اس مسبوق کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ (۲) اس حدیث کے اشارے سے بھی پتہ چلتا ہے کہ جس نے اول نماز نہیں پائی اسکی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر و قال : قال رسول الله : اذا أحدث الامام بعد ما يرفع رأسه من آخر سجدة و استوى جـالـسـا تـمـت صلوته ، و صلوة من خلفه ممن ائتم به ممن أدرك أول الصلوة (دار قطنی ، باب من أحدث قبل التسلیم ، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو شروع نماز سے ہے اسکی نماز بھی پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ اسکا مفہوم مخالف یہ ہے کہ جس نے شروع نماز نہیں پائی اسکی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔۔ حدث سے نماز فاسد ہو جائے اسکے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن على بن طلق قال قال رسول الله الله اذا فساء احدكم في الصلوة فلينصرف فليتوضأ وليعد الصلوة . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا حدث فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۵۱ نمبر ۲۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز میں حدث ہو جائے تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اور قہقہ مارنے سے نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی اور وضو بھی ٹوٹ جائے گا اسکے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔عن عمران بن حصین قال : سمعت رسول الله الله الله يقول : من ضحک فی الصلوة قرقرة فليعد الوضوء و الصلوة (دارقطنی، باب أحاديث القهقبته في الصلوة وعللها ، ج اول ص ۱۷۲، نمبر ۶۰۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قہقہہ مار کر ہنسے گا تو نماز بھی ٹوٹے گی اور وضو بھی ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
And the loud laughter of the imam of the masbuq and his intentional hadath after the final sitting. Translation: (547) The imam of the masbuq laughing loudly after the final sitting, or intentionally breaking wudu. Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that if one intentionally breaks wudu before the final sitting, the prayer becomes invalid; but if after the final sitting, the prayer is completed with karahah. The scenario: After the final sitting, the imam of the masbuq laughed loudly or intentionally broke wudu, then his prayer is completed with karahah because no fard remains. But the masbuq's prayer is still in the middle; he still has one more rak'ah to pray, so his prayer becomes invalid. (1) The reason is that when the imam committed hadath, his prayer became invalid, but all fards were already completed, so there was no need to rebuild; therefore it was considered completed with deficiency. But the masbuq's prayer still remains and his fards are still due; and in between, the imam committed hadath, so in reality, due to the invalidity of the imam's prayer, the masbuq's prayer also becomes invalid. (2) An indication from this hadith also shows that one who did not catch the beginning of the prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. The hadith: From Abdullah bin Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah said: When the imam breaks wudu after raising his head from the last sajda and sitting upright, his prayer is complete, and the prayer of those behind him who caught the beginning of the prayer. (Darqutni). This hadith states that the one who is from the beginning, his prayer is also complete. Its opposite meaning is that the one who did not catch the beginning, his prayer becomes invalid. For the invalidation of prayer by hadath, there is a hadith: From Ali bin Talq who said: The Messenger of Allah said: If any of you passes wind during prayer, let him leave, make wudu, and repeat the prayer. (Abu Dawud). This hadith states that if hadath occurs during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid. And for laughter breaking prayer, there is a hadith: From Imran bin Husayn who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Whoever laughs loudly (qarqara) in prayer, let him repeat wudu and the prayer. (Darqutni). From this hadith, it is learned that if one laughs loudly, both prayer and wudu break.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of the imam's loud laughter (qahqaha) or intentional hadath after the final sitting on the congregation, specifically the masbuq. The ruling distinguishes between before and after the final sitting. For the imam himself, if he laughs or commits hadath after the final sitting, his prayer is considered complete (with karahah) because all fard acts are done. However, for the masbuq, since he has an incomplete prayer (needs one more rak'ah), the imam's action invalidates his prayer because the imam's prayer becomes invalid at that moment, and the masbuq's prayer remains connected to the imam's. The passage supports this with hadiths: one about the imam's hadath after the final sitting only affecting those who didn't catch the beginning, and others establishing that hadath and loud laughter invalidate prayer and wudu.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter that disrupts prayer and wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Imam's prayer is valid with karahah; masbuq's prayer is valid.
C) Imam's prayer is valid with karahah; masbuq's prayer is invalid.
D) Imam's prayer is invalid; masbuq's prayer is valid.

Key Takeaway
The imam's hadath after the final sitting completes his prayer with karahah but invalidates the masbuq's prayer.

Mistaken Tasleem After Two Rak'ahs: Forgetful vs Intentional
Ruling on mistaken tasleem after two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between forgetful and intentional mistaken tasleem after two rak'ahs and state the ruling for each case, including the condition for bina'.

Core Idea
Intentional termination of prayer based on mistaken assumption invalidates; forgetfulness permits building if no nullifier occurs.

In the Hanafi school, making tasleem early in a prayer can have different consequences depending on the reason. This passage clarifies that if you mistakenly think you are a traveler or that the prayer has only two rak'ahs, your ruling changes based on whether the error was forgetful or deliberate. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correcting prayers and avoiding invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize the difference between forgetful tasleem (due to actual forgetfulness) and intentional tasleem based on a mistaken assumption (e.g., thinking you are a traveler or that it's a two-rak'ah prayer).
2
Apply the condition for bina'
For forgetful tasleem, determine whether any nullifier (turning chest from qibla, speaking, or hadath) occurred before attempting to build. If not, bina' is allowed.
If nullifier occurred, bina' is not allowed and the prayer must be restarted.
3
Determine the ruling for intentional tasleem
If the tasleem was deliberate (even with a mistaken belief), the prayer is broken and cannot be built upon. The intention was to terminate, not forgetfulness.
4
Synthesize the outcome
State the final ruling: forgetful with bina' before nullifiers → prayer valid with sajda sahw; intentional → prayer invalid, must restart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسلام على رأس ركعتين فى غير الثنائية ظانا انه مسافرا وانها الجمعة او انّها التراويح. ترجمه : (۵۴۸) دو رکعت سے زیادہ نمازوں میں دو ہی رکعت پر سلام پھیر دینا یہ گمان کرتے ہوئے کہ وہ مسافر ہے، یا یہ کہ وہ جمعہ ہے، یا تروایح ہے حالانکہ وہ عشاء کی نماز تھی ، یا ابھی ابھی مسلمان ہوا تھا اس لئے گمان کیا کہ دو ہی رکعت فرض ہے۔ تشریح : یہاں اصول الگ الگ ہیں [1] اگر بھول کر دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو قبلے سے سینہ پھرنے ، اور بات کرنے ، یا حدث کرنے سے پہلے پہلے تک بنا کر سکتا ہے، مثلا ظہر کی نماز تھی اور بھول سے دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو سینہ پھر نے اور بات کرنے ، یا حدث کرنے سے پہلے پہلے تک بنا کرے اور مزید دو رکعت ملا کر سجدہ سہو کرے اور نماز پوری کر لے ۔ (۲) لیکن اگر بھول کر سلام نہیں پھیرا بلکہ مسافر سمجھ کر یا جمع سمجھ کر، یا یہ سمجھا کہ تراویح کی نماز ہے حالانکہ وہ عشاء کی نماز تھی ، اور جان کر سلام پھیر دیا تو اب نماز ٹوٹ گئی، بنا نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسی طرح نو مسلم تھا ، اس کو معلوم نہیں تھا کہ ظہر کی چار رکعت ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس نے دورکعت ہی پر سلام پھیر دیا تو اب بنا نہیں کرسکتا۔ وجه : (۱) یہاں بھول کر سلام نہیں پھیرا ہے بلکہ جان کر مکمل انقطاع کی نیت سے سلام پھیرا ہے، اس لئے بنا نہیں کر سکتا۔
And making tasleem after two rak'ahs in non-two-rak'ah prayers, thinking he is a traveler, or that it is Friday, or that it is tarawih. Translation: (548) Making tasleem after two rak'ahs in prayers of more than two rak'ahs, thinking he is a traveler, or that it is Friday, or tarawih, when in fact it was Isha prayer, or he was a new Muslim and thought only two rak'ahs were fard. Explanation: Here the principles are separate: [1] If he made tasleem forgetfully after two rak'ahs, then before turning his chest from the qibla, speaking, or committing hadath, he can build upon it. For example, if it was Zuhr prayer and he forgetfully made tasleem after two rak'ahs, then before turning his chest, speaking, or hadath, he can build, perform two more rak'ahs, do sajda sahw, and complete the prayer. (2) But if he did not make tasleem forgetfully, rather thinking he is a traveler, or thinking it is Friday, or thinking it is tarawih (while it was Isha), and he made tasleem deliberately, then the prayer is broken; he cannot build. Similarly, a new Muslim who did not know that Zuhr has four rak'ahs and made tasleem after two rak'ahs — he cannot build. Reason: (1) Here he did not make tasleem forgetfully, but deliberately with the intention of complete disconnection, so he cannot build.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two scenarios: unintentional (forgetful) and intentional tasleem after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer. If forgetful, the person can rebuild the prayer (bina') by adding the remaining rak'ahs and performing sajda sahw, provided no turning away, speech, or hadath occurred. If intentional, based on a mistaken assumption (e.g., thinking he is a traveler or it's a two-rak'ah prayer), the prayer is invalid and cannot be built upon. The reason is that the intention was to completely terminate the prayer, not due to forgetfulness.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Building upon a prayer by adding missed parts without restarting, permitted in forgetfulness before certain nullifiers.
سلام (tasleem): The concluding salutation of prayer, saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to the right and left.
سجدہ سہو (sajda sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for mistakes in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgetfully makes tasleem after two rak'ahs in Zuhr and then immediately turns his chest away from the qibla before realizing his mistake, what is the ruling?
A) He can build upon the prayer and complete it.
B) His prayer is invalid and he must restart.
C) He can continue but must perform sajda sahw only.
D) His prayer is valid as two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
The ability to build upon a mistaken early tasleem depends on whether the tasleem was forgetful and whether any nullifier occurred before building.

Imam's Hadath After Final Sajdah: Effect on Ma'mum
Ruling with proof on effect of imam's hadath on masbuq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's prayer and the masbuq's prayer when the imam has hadath after the final sajdah, and explain the dalil from the hadith using mafhum al-mukhalafah.

Core Idea
Imam's prayer valid; masbuq's prayer invalid after imam's post-sajdah hadath.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in congregational prayer: what happens if the imam loses wudu after the final prostration but before salam? The Hanafi school distinguishes between followers who caught the beginning of the prayer and those who joined late (masbuq). The ruling is based on the completion of obligatory acts (fara'id) and a prophetic hadith. We will explore the reasoning and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam experiences hadath (ritual impurity) after raising his head from the final sajdah and sitting upright, but before saying the salam. Determine the status of his prayer and that of the followers.
The timing is crucial: after the final sajdah, all obligatory acts (fara'id) are complete for the imam.
2
Apply the Hanafi ruling
State the Hanafi position: the imam's prayer is valid (sahih) because the fara'id are done. However, the prayer of a masbuq (latecomer) who has not yet completed his own fara'id becomes invalid (batil).
The masbuq's prayer is still in progress and depends on the imam's valid prayer.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The imam's prayer is considered complete with deficiency; no need to rebuild (bina'). The masbuq's prayer is incomplete, and the imam's invalidity transfers to the follower because the follower still needs the imam.
The principle: the follower's prayer is connected to the imam's prayer for the missed portion.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar states: 'When the imam has hadath after raising his head from the last sajdah and sits upright, his prayer is complete, and the prayer of those behind him who caught the beginning of the prayer (is complete).' The mafhum al-mukhalafah indicates that those who did not catch the beginning have their prayer invalid.
The hadith is from Dar Qutni, ahad transmission (zanni al-thubut), but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalalah) for Hanafis.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that the masbuq is not affected by the imam's hadath if he had already commenced his own prayer with the imam. This highlights the importance of the Hanafi reliance on mafhum al-mukhalafah.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه : (۱) اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ امام نے جب حدث کیا تو امام کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو گئی تھی لیکن تمام فرائض پورے ہو گئے تھے اسلئے دوبارہ بناء کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں رہی ، اسلئے نقص کے ساتھ نماز پوری سمجھ لی گئی۔ لیکن مسبوق کی نماز ابھی باقی ہے اور اسکے فرائض بھی باقی ہیں اور اسکے درمیان ہی میں امام نے حدث کر دیا تو حقیقت میں امام کی نماز فاسد ہونے کی وجہ سے اس مسبوق کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ (۲) اس حدیث کے اشارے سے بھی پتہ چلتا ہے کہ جس نے اول نماز نہیں پائی اسکی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر و قال : قال رسول الله : اذا أحدث الامام بعد ما يرفع رأسه من آخر سجدة و استوى جـالـسـا تـمـت صلوته ، و صلوة من خلفه ممن ائتم به ممن أدرك أول الصلوة (دار قطنی ، باب من أحدث قبل التسلیم ، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۸ نمبر ۱۴۰۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو شروع نماز سے ہے اسکی نماز بھی پوری ہو جائے گی ۔ اسکا مفہوم مخالف یہ ہے کہ جس نے شروع نماز نہیں پائی اسکی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
Explanation (1): The reason for this is that when the imam had a hadath, the imam's prayer also became invalid, but all the obligatory parts (fara'id) had been completed, so there was no need to rebuild (bina') again. Therefore, the prayer was considered complete with deficiency. But the prayer of the ma'mum who missed the beginning (masbuq) is still remaining, and his obligatory parts are also remaining. In the middle of his prayer, the imam committed hadath, so in reality, because the imam's prayer became invalid, this masbuq's prayer will also become invalid. (2) This hadith also indicates that the one who did not catch the beginning of the prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. The hadith is: From Abdullah ibn Umar (ra) who said: The Messenger of Allah (saw) said: When the imam has hadath after raising his head from the last sajdah and sits upright, his prayer is complete, and the prayer of those behind him who followed him and caught the beginning of the prayer (is complete). (Dar Qutni, Chapter on one who has hadath before salam, vol. 1, p. 1368, no. 1409) This hadith states that the one who was present from the beginning of the prayer, his prayer also becomes complete. Its opposite meaning is that the one who did not catch the beginning of the prayer, his prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling regarding the effect of the imam's hadath (ritual impurity) after the final prostration but before salam. The passage type is a ruling with proof (dalil). The text explains that if the imam experiences hadath after the final sajdah and sitting upright, his own prayer is considered complete because all obligatory acts (fara'id) have been performed. However, a masbuq (one who joined the prayer late) still has remaining rak'as to complete. Since the imam's prayer is invalidated by the hadath, the masbuq's prayer also becomes invalid because the imam's prayer is no longer valid to follow. The hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar is cited as evidence. The hadith explicitly states that the prayer of the imam and those who caught the beginning is complete, implying by its opposite meaning (mafhum mukhalaf) that those who did not catch the beginning have their prayer invalidated. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and is based on the principle that the imam's invalidity affects the follower only if the follower still needs the imam.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has already begun, missing one or more rak'as.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, such as passing wind, urine, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this lesson, what is the status of a follower who caught the beginning of the prayer when the imam has hadath after the final sajdah?
A) His prayer becomes invalid.
B) His prayer is complete and valid.
C) His prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.
D) He must repeat the prayer from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
The imam's hadath after the final sajdah completes his prayer but invalidates the masbuq's prayer due to the latter's incomplete fara'id.

Loud Laughter Invalidates Prayer and Wudu
States ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on loud laughter in prayer, explain the dalil (proof) from the hadith, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of other schools.

Core Idea
Loud laughter (qahqaha) in prayer invalidates both the salah and the wudu — a distinctive Hanafi ruling.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: that audible laughter during prayer nullifies not only the prayer but also the state of wudu. This ruling is based on a hadith narrated by Imran ibn Husayn. We will analyze the proof, understand the Hanafi methodology of istidlal, and note the cross-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Loud laughter (qahqaha) during prayer. The ruling: both the prayer and the wudu become invalid (batil).
The Arabic term used is qahqaha or qarqara, meaning audible laughter.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is a hadith from Imran ibn Husayn (ra), recorded by Dar Qutni. The Prophet (saw) says: 'Whoever laughs loudly in prayer, let him repeat the wudu and the prayer.'
The hadith is a Sunnah ahad, so its thubut (transmission) is zanni, but its dalala (meaning) is considered qati (clear) by Hanafis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fal yu'id' (let him repeat) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. Therefore, both wudu and prayer must be repeated, proving they are invalidated.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the command indicates obligation).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools, such as the Shafi'i, hold that laughter only invalidates the prayer, not the wudu. Their proof may differentiate between types of laughter or consider the wudu still valid.
This is a mukhtalaf fih (disputed) ruling.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on this hadith as a clear text (nass) and sees no conflicting evidence to override its apparent meaning. The ruling is established in Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists; all major Hanafi imams agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور قہقہ مارنے سے نماز ٹوٹ جائے گی اور وضو بھی ٹوٹ جائے گا اسکے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔عن عمران بن حصین قال : سمعت رسول الله الله الله يقول : من ضحک فی الصلوة قرقرة فليعد الوضوء و الصلوة (دارقطنی، باب أحاديث القهقبته في الصلوة وعللها ، ج اول ص ۱۷۲، نمبر ۶۰۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قہقہہ مار کر ہنسے گا تو نماز بھی ٹوٹے گی اور وضو بھی ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
And from laughing loudly (qahqaha), the prayer will break, and also the wudu will break. For this, there is a hadith: From Imran ibn Husayn (ra) who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (saw) say: Whoever laughs loudly (qarqara) in prayer, let him repeat the wudu and the prayer. (Dar Qutni, Chapter on Hadith about qahqaha in prayer and its defects, vol. 1, p. 172, no. 602) From this hadith, it is known that if one laughs loudly, both the prayer and the wudu will break.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling regarding loud laughter in prayer. The lesson type is a ruling with proof. The text states that laughing loudly (qahqaha/qarqara) invalidates both the prayer and the wudu. The hadith from Imran ibn Husayn is cited as evidence: the Prophet (saw) commanded to repeat both wudu and prayer after such laughter. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may hold that laughter only nullifies prayer, not wudu, or only nullifies prayer beyond a certain point. The key distinction is between faint laughter (which may not break wudu) and audible laughter (which breaks both). The hadith is considered authentic (sahih) by some scholars and is relied upon in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
قہقہہ / قرقرة (qahqaha / qarqara): Loud, audible laughter that can be heard by others, as opposed to a faint smile or chuckle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what effect does loud laughter (qahqaha) have during prayer?
A) Only the prayer becomes invalid.
B) Only the wudu becomes invalid.
C) Both prayer and wudu become invalid.
D) Neither prayer nor wudu becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Loud laughter (qahqaha) during prayer invalidates both the prayer and the wudu according to the Hanafi school, based on the clear imperative in the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn.

Intentional vs Forgetful Salam: Bina' and Its Limits
Ruling on saying salam after two raka'at thinking it's a two-raka'at prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between forgetful and intentional salam errors and apply the Hanafi rule of bina' to the correct scenario.

Core Idea
Forgetful salam can be fixed by bina'; intentional salam breaks the prayer completely.

This lesson tackles a common scenario: saying salam too early due to a mistaken assumption. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling that depends on the worshipper's intention. We will examine the proof from the hadith of Dhul-Yadain and understand the critical distinction between forgetfulness and intentional termination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and error type
Read the case: the worshipper says salam after two raka'at in a four-raka'at prayer. Determine whether the salam was said forgetfully or intentionally based on the worshipper's belief and state.
Forgetful = genuine memory lapse; intentional = deliberate action based on mistaken belief (e.g., thinking it's a two-raka'at prayer).
2
Determine the ruling based on intention
Apply the principle: if forgetful, bina' is allowed; if intentional, prayer is invalid (batil) and must be restarted.
The key is whether the worshipper intended to end the prayer completely (inqita').
3
Apply the Hanafi rule of bina' and sajda al-sahw
For forgetful salam: the worshipper can build by adding the remaining raka'at and performing sajda al-sahw, provided he has not turned his chest away, spoken, or invalidated wudu.
Bina' is a concession unique to Hanafi fiqh in many such cases.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that salam ends the prayer; even a forgetful salam invalidates it and requires restart. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
This difference arises from varying interpretations of the hadith and principles of continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۴۸) دو رکعت سے زیادہ نمازوں میں دو ہی رکعت پر سلام پھیر دینا یہ گمان کرتے ہوئے کہ وہ مسافر ہے، یا یہ کہ وہ جمعہ ہے، یا تروایح ہے حالانکہ وہ عشاء کی نماز تھی ، یا ابھی ابھی مسلمان ہوا تھا اس لئے گمان کیا کہ دو ہی رکعت فرض ہے۔ تشریح : یہاں اصول الگ الگ ہیں [1] اگر بھول کر دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو قبلے سے سینہ پھرنے ، اور بات کرنے ، یا حدث کرنے سے پہلے پہلے تک بنا کر سکتا ہے، مثلا ظہر کی نماز تھی اور بھول سے دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو سینہ پھر نے اور بات کرنے ، یا حدث کرنے سے پہلے پہلے تک بنا کرے اور مزید دو رکعت ملا کر سجدہ سہو کرے اور نماز پوری کر لے ۔ (۲) لیکن اگر بھول کر سلام نہیں پھیرا بلکہ مسافر سمجھ کر یا جمع سمجھ کر، یا یہ سمجھا کہ تراویح کی نماز ہے حالانکہ وہ عشاء کی نمازت تھی ، اور جان کر سلام پھیر دیا تو اب نماز ٹوٹ گئی، بنا نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسی طرح نو مسلم تھا ، اس کو معلوم نہیں تھا کہ ظہر کی چار رکعت ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس نے دورکعت ہی پر سلام پھیر دیا تو اب بنا نہیں کرسکتا۔ وجه : (۱) یہاں بھول کر سلام نہیں پھیرا ہے بلکہ جان کر مکمل انقطاع کی نیت سے سلام پھیرا ہے، اس لئے بنا نہیں کر سکتا۔ (۲) بھول کر سلام پھیرے تو بنا کر سکتا ہے، اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن ابی ھریرة قال صلى بنا النبي الله الظهر او صلى الله الـعـصـر فسلم فقال له ذو اليدين : الصلاة يا رسول الله أنقضت ؟ فقال النبى له لاصحابه احق ما يقول ؟ قالوا نعم فصلى ركعتين اخريين ثم سجد سجدتین ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذ اسلم فی رکعتین ص ۱۹۶، نمبر ۱۳۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بھول سے دورکعت پر سلام کر دیا تو دوبارہ اس پر بنا کیا۔ اصول : بھول کر سلام پھیرے تو بنا کر سکتا ہے۔ جان کر سلام پھیرے تو بنا نہیں کرسکتا۔
Translation: (548) Saying salam after two raka'at in prayers that have more than two raka'at, assuming that he is a traveler, or that it is Jumu'ah, or Tarawih, while it was the Isha prayer, or he was a recent convert so he assumed that two raka'at are fard. Explanation: Here the principles are separate. [1] If he forgetfully said salam after two raka'at, then before turning his chest away from the qibla, or speaking, or having hadath, he can build (bina). For example, it was Zuhr prayer and he forgetfully said salam after two raka'at, then before turning his chest away, speaking, or having hadath, he should build, join two more raka'at, perform sajda al-sahw, and complete his prayer. (2) But if he did not forgetfully say salam, rather he thought he was a traveler, or thought it was Jumu'ah, or thought it was Tarawih while it was Isha prayer, and said salam intentionally, then the prayer is broken; he cannot build. Similarly, if he was a new Muslim and did not know that Zuhr has four raka'at, so he said salam after two raka'at, then he cannot build. Explanation: (1) Here he did not say salam forgetfully, but said salam intentionally with the intention of complete disconnection, so he cannot build. (2) If he forgetfully says salam, he can build. For this, there is a hadith: From Abu Huraira who said: The Prophet (saw) led us in Zuhr or Asr prayer and said salam. Dhul-Yadain said to him: O Messenger of Allah, has the prayer been shortened? The Prophet (saw) said to his companions: Is it true what he says? They said: Yes. So he prayed two more raka'at and then performed two prostrations. (Bukhari, Chapter on when he says salam after two raka'at, p. 196, no. 1327) This hadith states that when he said salam forgetfully after two raka'at, he built upon it. Principle: If he says salam forgetfully, he can build. If he says salam intentionally, he cannot build.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed Hanafi ruling about saying salam after two raka'at in a prayer that normally has more than two (e.g., Zuhr, Asr, Isha). The lesson type is a ruling with proof. The matn (548) states the case: a person says salam after two raka'at under a mistaken assumption (thinking he is a traveler, or that it is Jumu'ah or Tarawih, or as a new Muslim ignorant of the number). The commentary distinguishes two scenarios: (1) Forgetful salam: the person can rebuild (bina) by adding the remaining raka'at and performing sajda al-sahw, provided he has not turned away from qibla, spoken, or had hadath. This is based on the hadith of Dhul-Yadain from Bukhari. (2) Intentional salam: if he consciously said salam due to a mistaken belief about the nature of the prayer, the prayer is invalid and cannot be rebuilt. This is because he intended to end the prayer completely. The rationale is that forgetfulness does not negate the continuity of prayer, while intentional termination does. The hadith of Dhul-Yadain is cited as evidence: the Prophet (saw) built upon his prayer after forgetfully saying salam at two raka'at. The principle summarizes: forgetful salam allows bina; intentional salam does not. This ruling is distinctive to Hanafi fiqh in its detailed application of bina'.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Building upon the existing prayer by adding the remaining raka'at after an error, without restarting from the beginning.
سجده سہو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for unintended omissions or additions in the prayer.
انقطاع (inqita'): Complete disconnection from the prayer, i.e., intending to end it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-raka'at prayer, if a person says salam after two raka'at thinking it is a two-raka'at prayer (e.g., due to being a new Muslim), what is the ruling?
A) He can build and complete the prayer.
B) He must restart the entire prayer.
C) His prayer is valid and he does nothing.
D) He performs sajda al-sahw only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between forgetful salam (bina' allowed) and intentional salam (prayer invalid), based on the hadith of Dhul-Yadain.

Forgetting Salam in Prayer: Building upon Mistake
Ruling on forgetfully ending prayer early and its rectification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetfully saying salam in prayer and apply the condition of forgetfulness to determine whether building (bina) is permitted.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness does not invalidate prayer; one can build upon a forgetful salam.

In this lesson, we examine a common oversight in prayer: accidentally ending it early. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on a Prophetic precedent. We will analyze the condition of forgetfulness and the mechanism of building (bina) to rectify the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forgetfully saying salam after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer. The ruling: the prayer remains valid, and one can build upon it by completing the remaining rak'ahs and performing sajdah al-sahw.
The two rak'ahs already performed are considered valid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira in Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet ﷺ forgetfully said salam after two rak'ahs, then completed the prayer after being reminded.
The hadith is from a reliable source (Bukhari, #1327).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of completing the prayer after forgetful salam indicates that the salam did not invalidate the prayer. The companions' affirmation confirms the permissibility of building upon the mistake.
The imperative to complete the prayer shows that building (bina) is the correct response.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and condition
The Hanafi school allows bina only if the early salam was forgetful. If intentional, the prayer is invalid and must be restarted. Some other schools may require repeating the entire prayer even for forgetfulness.
The condition of forgetfulness is crucial for the ruling.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario: if a person forgetfully says salam after two rak'ahs in Dhuhr prayer, he should stand up, complete the remaining two rak'ahs, and then perform sajdah al-sahw. The prayer is valid.
No need to repeat the whole prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلوة وهي العشاء او كان قريب عهد بالاسلام فظنّ الفرض ركعتين بھول کر سلام پھیرے تو بنا کر سکتا ہے، اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن ابی ھریرة قال صلى بنا النبي الله الظهر او صلى الله الـعـصـر فسلم فقال له ذو اليدين : الصلاة يا رسول الله أنقضت ؟ فقال النبى له لاصحابه احق ما يقول ؟ قالوا نعم فصلى ركعتين اخريين ثم سجد سجدتین ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذ اسلم فی رکعتین ص ۱۹۶، نمبر ۱۳۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بھول سے دورکعت پر سلام کر دیا تو دوبارہ اس پر بنا کیا۔ اصول : بھول کر سلام پھیرے تو بنا کر سکتا ہے۔ جان کر سلام پھیرے تو بنا نہیں کرسکتا۔
Chapter: What Invalidates Prayer. And it is the 'isha prayer, or he was recently converted to Islam and thought the obligatory prayer is two rak'ahs. If he forgetfully says salam, he can build upon it. The hadith for this is: from Abu Huraira that the Prophet ﷺ led us in Dhuhr or 'Asr prayer and said salam. Dhul-Yadain said: 'O Messenger of Allah, has the prayer been shortened?' The Prophet asked his companions: 'Is he right?' They said yes. So he prayed two more rak'ahs and then made two prostrations. (Bukhari, Chapter: When He Says Salam in Two Rak'ahs, p.196, no.1327) In this hadith, he forgot and said salam after two rak'ahs, so he built upon it again. Principle: If he forgetfully says salam, he can build. If he knowingly says salam, he cannot build.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling concerning a common mistake in prayer: prematurely ending the prayer by saying salam after only two rak'ahs. The text specifies two scenarios where this might occur: first, if the prayer is 'Isha (which normally has four rak'ahs) and the person forgets; second, if a new Muslim mistakenly thinks the obligatory prayer is two rak'ahs. The ruling is that if the salam was said out of forgetfulness (bhool), the prayer is not invalidated; rather, the person can build upon the prayer (bina karna) by completing the remaining rak'ahs and then performing the prostrations of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). The proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira where the Prophet ﷺ himself forgot and completed the prayer after being reminded. The key condition is that the salam must be forgetful; if one knowingly says salam early, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated from the beginning. This distinction is captured in the principle (asl): forgetfulness allows building, intentionality does not.

Key Terms
بنا (bina): Building upon the existing prayer by continuing from where one left off.
بھول (bhool): Forgetfulness; an unintentional error in action during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgetfully says salam after two rak'ahs in Dhuhr prayer, what should he do?
A) Repeat the entire prayer from the beginning.
B) Complete the remaining two rak'ahs and perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) The prayer is invalid and no action is needed.
D) Continue from where he left off without any extra prostrations.

Key Takeaway
A forgetful early salam does not invalidate the prayer; one must complete the missed rak'ahs and perform sajdah al-sahw.
